The Companions are the Best of Generations
Defines the superiority of the Companions and explains the term 'generations'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Companions are the best generation after the prophets, with a gradation in rank based on sacrifice and service.

Core Idea
Companions are the best of all generations, but not all are equal.

This lesson explores the first part of the poem where the author declares the Companions as the best generation. We will see the evidence from hadith and understand the meaning of 'generations' in this context.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp the main claim that the Companions are the best generation.
2
Identify the evidence
Note the two hadiths cited to support the superiority of Companions over all others except prophets.
3
Understand the gradation
Recognize that while all Companions are honored, those who fought and died under the Prophet's banner have a higher rank.
This shows that not all Companions are equal in rank.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النبوات [خيرُ القرون] ٧٥ - وصَحْبُهُ خَيْرُ القُرُونِ فَاسْتَمِعْ فَنابِمِيْ فَتابِعٌ لِمَنْ تَبِعْ قوله : ( وصَحْبُهُ خَيْرُ القُرُونِ) أي : وأصحابه أفضل القرون المتأخرة والمتقدمة ما عدا الأنبياء والرسل ؛ لحديث: إنَّ الله اختار أصحابي على العالمين سوى النبيين والمرسلين» (١) ، ولحديث: «الله الله في أصحابي لا تتخذوهم غَرَضاً من بعدي، فوالذي نفسي بيده لو أنفق أحدُكم مثلَ أُحدٍ ذهباً ما بلغَ مُدَّ أحدهم ولا نَصِيْفَهُ (۲) ، ولا يخفى ترجيحُ رُتبة مَنْ لازمه ، وقاتل معه، وقتل تحت رايته على من لم يكن كذلك، وإن كان شرف الصحبة حاصلاً للجميع. : والقُرون جمع قَرْن ومعناه أهل زمانٍ واحدٍ متقارب اشتركوا في أمرٍ من الأمور المقصودة، كالصحابة فإنهم اشتركوا في الصحبة وهكذا مَنْ بعدهم، وقيل: معناه: الزمن الذي اشترك أهله في الأمر المذكور، وسُمِّيَ قَرْناً لأنه يَقْرِنُ أُمَّةٌ بأمَّةٍ وعالماً بعالم وعلى الأول فلا تقدير في كلام المصنف، وعلى الثاني ففي كلامه تقدير مضاف؛ أي: أهل القرون كما قدَّره الشارح (۳) في حل المتن . وقوله : (فَاسْتَمِعْ) تكملة. وقوله : (فَتابِعِي) بإسكان الياء مخففة يفيد أن رتبة التابعين تلي رتبة الصحابة من غير تراخ كبير، ولذلك عبر بالفاء المفيدة للترتيب والتعقيب. والتابعي من اجتمع بالصحابي اجتماعاً متعارفاً، ولا يُشترط فيه طول الاجتماع كما في الصحابي مع النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ، وهذا ما صححه ابن الصلاح والنووي، وهو المعتمد. والطريقة المشهورة: أنه يُشترط التمييز في التابعي دون الصحابي، والمعتمد عندنا عدم اشتراطه في التابعي، كما لا يشترط في الصحابي .
The Prophecies [The best of generations] 75 - And his companions are the best of generations, so listen, then my followers [explanation:] 'And his companions are the best of generations' means: his Companions are the best of the later and earlier generations, except prophets and messengers; due to the hadith: 'Indeed Allah chose my Companions over all worlds except the prophets and messengers,' and due to the hadith: 'Allah, Allah concerning my Companions; do not make them targets after me. For by the One in whose hand my soul is, if any of you were to spend gold like Mount Uhud, it would not reach a mudd of one of them nor half of it.' And it is not hidden that the rank of one who accompanied him, fought with him, and was killed under his banner is preferred over one who was not like that, even though the honor of Companionship is attained by all. 'And generations' (al-qurūn) is the plural of qarn, meaning the people of one close time period who share in some intended matter, like the Companions who share in Companionship, and likewise those after them. And it is said: its meaning is the time period in which its people share in the mentioned matter. It is called qarn because it couples one nation with another and one scholar with another. On the first interpretation, there is no ellipsis in the author's speech; on the second, there is an ellipsis of a genitive construct, i.e., 'the people of the generations' as the commentator estimated in his explanation of the text. And his saying 'so listen' (fa-stamiʿ) is a supplement. And his saying 'then my followers' (fa-tābiʿī) with the yāʾ silent and lightened indicates that the rank of the Followers immediately follows the rank of the Companions without much delay, therefore it is expressed with the letter fā which indicates sequence and immediacy. And the Follower (al-tābiʿī) is one who met the Companion in a customary meeting, and prolonged association is not required there as it is for the Companion with the Prophet. This is what Ibn al-Ṣalāḥ and al-Nawawī corrected, and it is the relied-upon view. The well-known method is that discretion (tamyīz) is required in the Follower but not in the Companion, but the relied-upon view with us is that it is not required in the Follower, just as it is not required in the Companion.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage explains the meaning of the poetic line: 'And his companions are the best of generations, so listen, then my followers.' The author clarifies that 'his companions' refers to the Companions of the Prophet, and they are the best of all generations, both earlier and later, except for prophets and messengers. This is supported by two hadiths: one stating that Allah chose the Companions over all worlds except prophets, and another stating that no amount of charity from later generations can equal even a handful of what the Companions gave. The author notes that there is a gradation among the Companions: those who accompanied the Prophet in battles and were martyred under his banner have a higher rank, although all share the honor of companionship. Then the term 'qurūn' (generations) is defined: it refers to a group of people living in a close time period who share a common characteristic, like companionship for the Companions. Alternatively, it can mean the time period itself. The phrase 'fa-stamiʿ' (so listen) is a rhetorical supplement. The word 'fa-tābiʿī' (then my followers) with a lightened yāʾ indicates that the order of the Followers comes immediately after the Companions without a long interval, as signified by the letter fā. Finally, the definition of a Follower is given: one who met a Companion in a customary meeting, without the condition of prolonged association as required for being a Companion. The author mentions the scholarly dispute about requiring discretion (tamyīz) in a Follower but concludes that the relied-upon view is that it is not required, just as it is not required for a Companion.

Key Terms
صحابة
قرون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All Companions have the same rank.
Correction: The passage clarifies that those who fought and were martyred have a higher rank, though all share the honor of Companionship.

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited, how does the charity of later generations compare to that of the Companions?
A) It is greater.
B) It is equal.
C) It cannot reach even a handful of theirs.
D) It is accepted only if given in secret.

Key Takeaway
The Companions are the best generation after the prophets, with a hierarchy of honor based on their service and sacrifice.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Companions were chosen above all except prophets, how does your love and respect for them manifest in your daily actions? Are there times you speak of them with less than the utmost reverence? Commit to one specific change.
?
The passage tells us that not all Companions are equal in rank. Are you guilty of assuming that anyone who lived in that era is automatically equal in virtue? How might this affect your understanding of Islamic history and your own striving for closeness to Allah?
?
The Prophet warned not to make the Companions targets. Have you ever engaged in or tolerated criticism of any Companion? How can you actively defend their honor from today onward?

The Definition and Rank of the Followers
Clarifies the rank of the Followers and defines who is a Follower.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of a Follower, their rank immediately after the Companions, and the scholarly debate about the condition of discretion.

Core Idea
Followers directly succeed the Companions in rank and are defined by meeting a Companion, not by prolonged association.

This lesson continues the poem's explanation, focusing on the Followers. We learn that the word 'then' indicates their immediate succession, and we clarify the criteria for being a Follower.

Guided Path
1
Understand the word 'then'
Notice that the letter 'fā' in 'fa-tābiʿī' implies immediacy of rank, meaning the Followers come right after the Companions.
2
Define the Follower
Read the definition given by Ibn al-Ṣalāḥ and al-Nawawī: a Follower is one who met a Companion in a customary meeting.
Prolonged association is not required.
3
Examine the condition of discretion
Look at the two views: the well-known method requires discretion, but the relied-upon view does not require it for a Follower.
This shows flexibility in the definition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النبوات [خيرُ القرون] ٧٥ - وصَحْبُهُ خَيْرُ القُرُونِ فَاسْتَمِعْ فَنابِمِيْ فَتابِعٌ لِمَنْ تَبِعْ قوله : ( وصَحْبُهُ خَيْرُ القُرُونِ) أي : وأصحابه أفضل القرون المتأخرة والمتقدمة ما عدا الأنبياء والرسل ؛ لحديث: إنَّ الله اختار أصحابي على العالمين سوى النبيين والمرسلين» (١) ، ولحديث: «الله الله في أصحابي لا تتخذوهم غَرَضاً من بعدي، فوالذي نفسي بيده لو أنفق أحدُكم مثلَ أُحدٍ ذهباً ما بلغَ مُدَّ أحدهم ولا نَصِيْفَهُ (۲) ، ولا يخفى ترجيحُ رُتبة مَنْ لازمه ، وقاتل معه، وقتل تحت رايته على من لم يكن كذلك، وإن كان شرف الصحبة حاصلاً للجميع. : والقُرون جمع قَرْن ومعناه أهل زمانٍ واحدٍ متقارب اشتركوا في أمرٍ من الأمور المقصودة، كالصحابة فإنهم اشتركوا في الصحبة وهكذا مَنْ بعدهم، وقيل: معناه: الزمن الذي اشترك أهله في الأمر المذكور، وسُمِّيَ قَرْناً لأنه يَقْرِنُ أُمَّةٌ بأمَّةٍ وعالماً بعالم وعلى الأول فلا تقدير في كلام المصنف، وعلى الثاني ففي كلامه تقدير مضاف؛ أي: أهل القرون كما قدَّره الشارح (۳) في حل المتن . وقوله : (فَاسْتَمِعْ) تكملة. وقوله : (فَتابِعِي) بإسكان الياء مخففة يفيد أن رتبة التابعين تلي رتبة الصحابة من غير تراخ كبير، ولذلك عبر بالفاء المفيدة للترتيب والتعقيب. والتابعي من اجتمع بالصحابي اجتماعاً متعارفاً، ولا يُشترط فيه طول الاجتماع كما في الصحابي مع النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ، وهذا ما صححه ابن الصلاح والنووي، وهو المعتمد. والطريقة المشهورة: أنه يُشترط التمييز في التابعي دون الصحابي، والمعتمد عندنا عدم اشتراطه في التابعي، كما لا يشترط في الصحابي .

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A Follower must have prolonged association with a Companion.
Correction: The passage states that only a customary meeting is required, not prolonged association.

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon view regarding the condition of discretion (tamyīz) for a Follower?
A) It is required.
B) It is not required.
C) It is required only for Companions.
D) It is required for both.

Key Takeaway
A Follower is defined by a customary meeting with a Companion, not by prolonged association or discretion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage shows that a simple, customary meeting with a Companion could elevate a person to the rank of a Follower. In your life, do you seek out brief encounters with righteous people—scholars, elders, or pious individuals—with the same eagerness, knowing that even a short meeting can have a profound effect? What prevents you from doing so, and how will you change starting today?
?
If prolonged association is not required to be a Follower, then what does that say about the value of every moment spent with the righteous? Are there people in your circle who embody the Sunnah whom you have neglected to meet or listen to because you thought 'one conversation won't make a difference'? Reflect on a specific instance and commit to reaching out this week.
?
The relied-upon view removes the condition of discretion for a Follower, emphasizing that even a child who met a Companion could be a Follower. This humbles our understanding of spiritual rank—it is not based on intelligence or memory but on connection. Do you sometimes feel unworthy or inadequate to be counted among the followers of the Salaf because you think you lack knowledge or understanding? Let this lesson remind you that the core is simply meeting (figuratively today, through their teachings) and being connected. What step will you take today to strengthen that connection?

Two Conditions for Obligatory Interpretation
Author states the two conditions that make interpretation of reported conflicts obligatory.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two conditions that make interpretation of historical theological conflicts obligatory according to Ahl al-Sunnah methodology.

Core Idea
Interpretation is only required when the conflict is authentic and you know the details.

In this passage, the author explains when it becomes mandatory to interpret reported conflicts among the early scholars. Not every reported disagreement needs interpretation; there are clear conditions. As you read, note how the author excludes two categories from the obligation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the concise style and the use of 'al-awwal' and 'al-thani'.
2
Identify the two conditions
Find the two conditions listed. The first concerns the authenticity of the reported conflict. The second concerns the individual's knowledge of it.
The conditions are introduced with 'Shartān'.
3
Examine the exclusions
Notice what is excluded by each condition. The author explains what happens if each condition is not met.
The first exclusion leads to rejection; the second leads to non-obligation.
4
Reflect on the principle
Ask yourself why interpretation depends on knowledge. The passage explicitly states that interpretation is a branch of knowledge.
This connects to the broader principle in Islamic methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحاصل أن التأويل لا يجب إلا بشرطين : الأول : أن يكون التشاجر ثابتاً عند الأئمة بالأحاديث المتصلة الأسانيد. والثاني : أن يخوض الشخص فيه بأن يطلع على ما جرى بينهم. وخرج بالأول ما لم يثبت عند الأئمة، فهو مردود باطل، فنحكم عليه أنه مردود باطل، ولا يحتاج إلى تأويله، وخرج بالثاني ما ثبت عند الأئمة، لكن لم نطلع عليه ، فلا يجب تأويله أيضاً ؛ لأن تأويل الشيء فرع عن العلم به، والفرض أنه غير معلوم.
The conclusion is that interpretation is not obligatory except with two conditions: First: that the conflict be established with the imams through connected chains of narration (ahadith muttasila al-asaneed). Second: that the person delves into it by being aware of what occurred between them. The first condition excludes what is not established with the imams, for it is rejected and false, so we rule that it is rejected and false, and it does not need interpretation. The second condition excludes what is established with the imams but we have not been informed of it, so interpretation is not obligatory for that either, because interpretation of a thing is a branch of knowledge of it, and the assumption is that it is unknown.
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage clarifies the two conditions that make interpretation of reported conflicts obligatory. The author summarizes that interpretation is not required except under two conditions. First, the conflict must be authentically reported by the imams through connected chains of narration, meaning it is established historically beyond doubt. Second, the person must actually delve into the matter and become aware of what happened. If the report is not authentic, it is rejected and false, and no interpretation is needed. If it is authentic but the person has not studied it, then interpretation is also not obligatory because interpretation depends on knowledge.

Key Terms
التأويل
الأئمة
الأحاديث المتصلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Interpretation is always required for any reported conflict among scholars.
Correction: Interpretation is only obligatory when both conditions are met: the conflict is authentically reported and the person has studied it. Otherwise, it is not required.

Checkpoint
What does the first condition for obligatory interpretation require?
A) The person must be a scholar
B) The conflict must be established through connected chains of narration
C) The conflict must involve only the Prophet's family
D) The person must be a commoner

Key Takeaway
Interpretation of reported conflicts is only obligatory when the conflict is authentically documented and the individual has personal knowledge of the details.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear about a disagreement among scholars, do you immediately form an opinion without verifying the authenticity of the reports or studying the details? How does this lesson challenge you to pause and either remain silent or seek genuine knowledge before speaking?
?
Think of a time you judged a scholar's position based on a snippet you heard. In light of this passage, what would it look like to ‘delve into it’ before concluding? What are you willing to sacrifice to gain that knowledge?
?
This lesson says interpretation is only obligatory if the matter is known to you. What if many of the controversial topics in your mind are actually unknown to you? Will you admit that and let go of the need to have an opinion, or will you continue in speculation? Choose one topic today where you will either seek detailed knowledge or consciously remain silent.

Ruling on Delving into Companions' Disputes
Author explains the ruling on engaging with Sahaba disputes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that delving into the historical disputes among the Companions is not a religious obligation and is only permissible for specific authorized purposes.

Core Idea
Not all history is religious; some harms certainty.

This passage addresses a sensitive topic: the disputes that occurred among the Companions of the Prophet (peace be upon him). The author clarifies the proper stance: such discussions are not part of core Islamic creed, and in fact can be harmful. However, there are two legitimate reasons to engage with them: to refute those who misuse them, or for educational purposes. The common person is advised to avoid them entirely.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to get the author's own wording.
Notice the conditional 'if you delve into it' – this is not a command.
2
Identify the ruling
The author states that delving is not commanded, not part of creed, not beneficial, and may harm certainty. So the default is prohibition.
3
Find the exceptions
Two exceptions are given: refuting bigots (al-muta'assibin) and teaching (al-ta'lim). Note that teaching includes books with relevant reports.
4
Understand the rule for common people
Common people (al-awamm) are explicitly forbidden due to ignorance and lack of interpretive skill.
This shows the importance of knowledge and qualified scholarship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله : (إِنْ خُضْتَ فِيهِ) أي: إن قُدِّرَ أنك خضت فيه فأوله ولا تنقض أحداً وإنما قال المصنف ذلك لأن الشخص ليس مأموراً بالخوض فيما جرى بينهم، فإنه ليس من العقائد الدينية، ولا من القواعد الكلامية وليس مما يُنتفع به في الدين، بل ربما ضرَّ في اليقين فلا يُباح الخوض فيه إلا للرد على المتعصبين أو للتعليم، كتدريس الكتب التي تشتمل على الآثار المتعلقة بذلك، وأما العوام فلا يجوز لهم الخوض فيه ؛ لشدة جهلهم وعدم معرفتهم بالتأويل.
And his saying: 'If you delve into it' means: if it is assumed that you delve into it, then interpret it and do not defame anyone. The author only said that because a person is not commanded to delve into what occurred between them, for it is not part of religious beliefs, nor of kalam principles, and it is not something beneficial in religion. Rather, it may harm certainty, so it is not permissible to delve into it except to refute the bigots or for teaching, like teaching books that contain the reports related to that. As for the common people, they are not allowed to delve into it due to their severe ignorance and lack of knowledge of interpretation.
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling on engaging with the historical disputes among the Companions. The author interprets the phrase 'if you delve into it' as a conditional: if one does engage, then they must interpret positively and not speak ill of anyone. However, the author emphasizes that a person is not commanded to delve into these matters because they are not part of core religious creed, nor of kalam principles, and they do not benefit religion. In fact, they may harm one's certainty. Therefore, it is only permissible to delve into them for two purposes: to refute those who are biased (bigots) or for educational purposes, such as teaching books that contain these reports. As for the common people (al-awamm), they are forbidden from delving into these matters due to their severe ignorance and lack of knowledge of proper interpretation.

Key Terms
الخوض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think it is obligatory or beneficial to study all historical disputes among the Companions.
Correction: The passage clarifies that such topics are not part of core creed, may harm certainty, and are only permissible for specific purposes (refuting bigots or teaching). Common people must avoid them.

Checkpoint
For whom is it permissible to delve into the disputes among the Companions?
A) Anyone who wants to know history
B) Only scholars for refuting bigots or teaching
C) Common people
D) Only the caliphs

Key Takeaway
Delving into Companions' disputes is not part of Islamic creed; it is only permissible for refutation or teaching, and common people must avoid it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a story about a Companion that seems negative, do you immediately assume the worst or do you actively interpret it positively? How does this passage challenge your default reaction?
?
Have you ever engaged in discussions about Sahaba disputes out of curiosity? What would it cost you to stop and instead focus on what builds certainty?
?
If common people are forbidden from delving due to ignorance, are you truly qualified to interpret these reports? How does this affect your responsibility when sharing such knowledge?

The Ruling on Interpreting Sahaba Disputes
Sanusi defines the ruling on discussing Sahaba disputes and its exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the proper approach to discussing disputes among the Companions and when it is permissible to delve into those topics.

Core Idea
Interpret Sahaba disputes favorably and avoid delving except for teaching or refuting bigotry.

Sanusi explains that the disputes among the Companions must be interpreted in a good light, preserving their justice as mujtahids. He clarifies that delving into these matters is not part of religious beliefs and is generally prohibited, with two exceptions: to refute extremists or for educational purposes. This lesson outlines those boundaries and their rationale.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on interpretation
The passage states that the intended meaning of 'ta'wil' is to direct events to a good interpretation to improve one's opinion of the Companions. No Companion lost their justice because they were mujtahids.
Notice the emphasis on 'mujtahids' – their sincerity is assumed.
2
Understand the condition 'If you delve into it'
The author says if you do delve, then interpret favorably and do not disparage anyone. The default is not to delve at all because it is not beneficial and may harm certainty.
3
Identify the permissible exceptions
Delving is allowed only for refuting the bigoted (al-muta'assibin) or for teaching, such as teaching books containing relevant reports. The common people are absolutely forbidden from delving.
The common people are excluded due to ignorance and lack of interpretive ability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمراد من تأويل ذلك أن يُصرف إلى مَحمَلٍ حسن لتحسين الظن بهم، فلم يخرج واحد منهم عن العدالة بما وقع بينهم؛ لأنهم مجتهدون. وقوله : (إِنْ خُضْتَ فِيهِ) أي: إن قُدِّرَ أنك خضت فيه فأوله ولا تنقض أحداً وإنما قال المصنف ذلك لأن الشخص ليس مأموراً بالخوض فيما جرى بينهم، فإنه ليس من العقائد الدينية، ولا من القواعد الكلامية وليس مما يُنتفع به في الدين، بل ربما ضرَّ في اليقين فلا يُباح الخوض فيه إلا للرد على المتعصبين أو للتعليم، كتدريس الكتب التي تشتمل على الآثار المتعلقة بذلك، وأما العوام فلا يجوز لهم الخوض فيه ؛ لشدة جهلهم وعدم معرفتهم بالتأويل.

قوله : (واجْتَنِبْ دَاءَ الحَسَدٌ ) (۱) أي : واترك وجوباً في حال خوضك فيما شجر الحسد، فالإضافة للبيان إن أريد الداء المعنوي، أو الحسد الشبيه بالداء، فالإضافة من إضافة المشبه به للمشبه إن أُريد الداء الحسي، والمراد داء الحسد الحامل على الميل مع أحد الطرفين على وجه غير مرضي وقد قال : «الله الله في أصحابي لا تتخذوهم غَرَضاً بعدي مَنْ آذاهم فقد آذاني، ومَنْ آذاني فقد آذى الله ، ومَنْ آذى الله يُوشك أن يأخذَهُ (۲) ؛ أي: اتقوا الله ثم اتقوا الله، أو أنشدكم ثم أنشدكم الله في حق أصحابي وتعظيمهم لا تتخذوهم كالغَرَض الذي يُرمى إليه ،بالسهام فترموهم بالكلمات التي لا تناسب مقامهم، فمن آذاهم فقد آذاني، ومن آذاني فقد آذى الله ؛ أي: تعدى حدودَهُ ،وخالَفَهُ، ففيه مُشاكلةٌ، وإلا فحقيقة الإيذاء على الله محالة، آذى الله يُوشك أن يأخذه ؛ أي: يقرب أن يعذبه .

(۱) قوله : ( واجتنب داء الحسد) أي : حسد أحد الفريقين المتشاجرين، الحامل ذلك الحسد على الميل للفريق الآخر على وجه غير مرضي ؛ بأن يشتمل ذلك الميل على سبب غيره . هذا ما أراده المحشي. ثم الظاهر أن الحسد بمعناه الأصلي الذي هو تمني زوال نعمة الغير ليس مراداً هنا، بل المراد به هنا مطلق الإيذاء والسب والمعنى حينئذ : واجتنب سب الصحابة، هذا ما ظهر. انتهى أجهوري.

وفي رواية: «لا تسبوا أصحابي، مَنْ سبَّ أصحابي فعليه لعنة الله والملائكة والناس أجمعين، لا يقبلُ الله منه صَرْفاً ولا عَدْلاً (١) ، ومعلوم (۲) جواز لَعْنِ غيرِ المعين من العصاة والصرف الفرضُ، والعدلُ النقلُ . وقيل : بالعكس، وقيل غير ذلك، وهذا في المستحل، أو خارج مخرج المبالغة في الزَّجْر .
And the intended meaning of interpreting that is to direct it to a good interpretation to improve opinion of them, so none of them left justice due to what occurred between them because they are mujtahids. And His statement: (If you delve into it) means: if it is determined that you delved into it, then interpret it and do not disparage anyone. And the author only said that because a person is not commanded to delve into what happened between them, for it is not from religious beliefs nor from the principles of kalam (al-qawa'id al-kalamiyya) and is not something beneficial in religion, rather perhaps it harms certainty, so delving into it is not permitted except to refute the bigoted or for teaching, like teaching books that contain the reports related to that. As for the common people, they are not allowed to delve into it due to their intense ignorance and lack of knowledge of interpretation. His statement: (And avoid the disease of envy) (1) means: and leave, obligatorily, in your state of delving into what occurred, envy; the addition is for clarification if the spiritual disease is intended, or envy resembling the disease, so the addition is of the likened to the like if the physical disease is intended. And what is meant is the disease of envy that drives one to incline with one of the two parties in an unapproved manner. And he said: 'By Allah, by Allah, regarding my Companions, do not take them as targets after me. Whoever harms them has harmed me, and whoever harms me has harmed Allah, and whoever harms Allah is likely to be seized (2); meaning: fear Allah, then fear Allah, or I implore you then implore you by Allah regarding the right of my Companions and their veneration. Do not make them like a target that is shot at with arrows, so you shoot them with words that are not befitting their station. So whoever harms them harms me, and whoever harms me harms Allah; meaning: he transgresses His limits and disobeys Him. In this there is a similarity (mushakala), otherwise the reality of harming Allah is impossible. 'And whoever harms Allah is likely to be seized' means: He is likely to punish him. (1) His statement: (And avoid the disease of envy) meaning: envy of one of the two disputing groups, that envy causing inclination towards the other group in an unapproved manner, such that that inclination includes a cause other than it. This is what the commentator intended. Then it appears that envy in its original sense of wishing for removal of another's blessing is not intended here, but here what is meant is absolute harm and reviling, and the meaning then is: avoid reviling the Companions. This is what appeared. End of remarks by al-Ujhuri. And in a narration: 'Do not revile my Companions; whoever reviles my Companions has upon him the curse of Allah, the angels, and all people. Allah will not accept from him any exchange (sarfan) or compensation (adlan) (1). And it is known (2) the permissibility of cursing a non-specific sinner. And 'sarf' is the obligatory act, and 'adl' is the supererogatory act. It is said the opposite, and other things said. This is concerning one who deems it permissible, or it is taken as an expression of hyperbolic deterrent.
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage is an explanatory commentary on the author's original lines regarding the interpretation of disputes among the Companions and the command to avoid envy. The author first clarifies that the proper interpretation of any difficult event among the Companions is to ascribe it a good meaning to maintain a good opinion of them, asserting that none of them lost their justice (adala) because they were all mujtahids. Then he explains the phrase 'If you delve into it' — meaning if you find yourself having to engage in discussing what happened among the Companions, then you should interpret it favorably and not disparage anyone. He justifies that the author only said this because a person is not commanded to delve into these disputes at all. He provides three reasons: (1) it is not part of religious beliefs, (2) it is not from the principles of kalam, and (3) it is not beneficial in religion; rather it may harm certainty. Therefore, delving is not permitted except for specific purposes: refuting the bigoted (al-muta'assibin) or for teaching, such as teaching books containing relevant reports. For the common people, it is absolutely forbidden due to their ignorance and lack of ability to interpret. Next, the author comments on the phrase 'And avoid the disease of envy.' He explains that this means: if you do delve (though discouraged), you must avoid envy. He then delves into the Arabic grammar of the phrase 'disease of envy' — whether the addition is for clarification or likening. The intended meaning is the envy that causes one to incline towards one party in an unapproved manner. Then he cites a hadith: 'By Allah, by Allah, regarding my Companions, do not take them as targets after me. Whoever harms them harms me...' He explains this hadith, noting that the apparent meaning of harming Allah is impossible, so it is a form of figurative language (mushakala) meaning transgression and disobedience. He also explains the expression 'is likely to be seized' as imminent punishment. The passage then includes a marginal note (from al-Ujhuri) clarifying that the word 'envy' here does not mean its literal sense of wishing removal of blessings, but rather absolute harm and insult, so the command is to avoid insulting the Companions. Finally, the author presents another hadith: 'Do not revile my Companions...' and explains the meaning of 'sarf' and 'adl' (obligatory and supererogatory acts, or vice versa), noting that the severe punishment is for one who deems reviling lawful or is a hyperbolic deterrent.

Key Terms
الصحابة
التأويل
الخوض
العدالة
المجتهدون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That discussing Sahaba disputes is a praiseworthy act of scholarship for anyone.
Correction: It is generally prohibited; only allowed for specific purposes like refuting bigotry or teaching scholars.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, for whom is it permitted to delve into the disputes among the Companions?
A) For every Muslim seeking knowledge
B) For the common people (al-'awamm)
C) For the purpose of refuting the bigoted or for teaching
D) For anyone who wishes to know the truth

Key Takeaway
The disputes among the Companions must be interpreted favorably, and delving into them is generally prohibited, allowed only for refuting bigotry or teaching.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a negative report about a Companion, does your mind immediately rush to judge them, or do you actively seek a good interpretation as Sanusi commands? What does your reaction reveal about your love for the Prophet's companions?
?
Are you ever tempted to discuss historical disputes among the Sahaba for entertainment or out of idle curiosity? How does this lesson expose that impulse as harmful to your certainty? Will you commit to avoiding such discussions except when necessary to defend or teach?
?
If you ever find yourself teaching about these matters, do you do so only to refute bigotry or to instill correct belief, or do you sometimes indulge in unnecessary details? How can you ensure your teaching aligns with the exceptions Sanusi allows?

Avoiding Envy and Harming the Companions
Sanusi warns against envy and harming the Companions, citing hadiths.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the prohibition of envying or harming the Companions and the severe warning against reviling them.

Core Idea
Envy and harm towards the Companions are forbidden, and insulting them incurs severe punishment.

Sanusi continues with a command to avoid the 'disease of envy,' explaining that it refers to any form of harm or insult towards the Companions. He then cites a prophetic hadith that equates harming them with harming Allah, using figurative language to emphasize the gravity. This lesson unpacks the meaning of envy in this context and the stern warning against reviling the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Understand the command to avoid envy
Read the passage: 'And avoid the disease of envy.' The author explains that this is an obligatory avoidance, and the 'disease' here is not literal envy but rather the inclination to harm one party unjustly.
The term 'envy' is used figuratively for harm and insult.
2
Analyze the first hadith
The hadith: 'By Allah, by Allah, regarding my Companions, do not take them as targets...' The commentary explains that harming them is likened to harming Allah through mushabaha (figurative similarity). The punishment is imminent.
3
Examine the second hadith on reviling
Another hadith: 'Do not revile my Companions; whoever reviles them incurs the curse of Allah...' The passage discusses the meaning of 'sarf' and 'adl' and notes that this applies to those who deem reviling lawful or is a hyperbolic deterrent.

Commentary
This passage is an explanatory commentary on the author's original lines regarding the interpretation of disputes among the Companions and the command to avoid envy. The author first clarifies that the proper interpretation of any difficult event among the Companions is to ascribe it a good meaning to maintain a good opinion of them, asserting that none of them lost their justice (adala) because they were all mujtahids. Then he explains the phrase 'If you delve into it' — meaning if you find yourself having to engage in discussing what happened among the Companions, then you should interpret it favorably and not disparage anyone. He justifies that the author only said this because a person is not commanded to delve into these disputes at all. He provides three reasons: (1) it is not part of religious beliefs, (2) it is not from the principles of kalam, and (3) it is not beneficial in religion; rather it may harm certainty. Therefore, delving is not permitted except for specific purposes: refuting the bigoted (al-muta'assibin) or for teaching, such as teaching books containing relevant reports. For the common people, it is absolutely forbidden due to their ignorance and lack of ability to interpret. Next, the author comments on the phrase 'And avoid the disease of envy.' He explains that this means: if you do delve (though discouraged), you must avoid envy. He then delves into the Arabic grammar of the phrase 'disease of envy' — whether the addition is for clarification or likening. The intended meaning is the envy that causes one to incline towards one party in an unapproved manner. Then he cites a hadith: 'By Allah, by Allah, regarding my Companions, do not take them as targets after me. Whoever harms them harms me...' He explains this hadith, noting that the apparent meaning of harming Allah is impossible, so it is a form of figurative language (mushakala) meaning transgression and disobedience. He also explains the expression 'is likely to be seized' as imminent punishment. The passage then includes a marginal note (from al-Ujhuri) clarifying that the word 'envy' here does not mean its literal sense of wishing removal of blessings, but rather absolute harm and insult, so the command is to avoid insulting the Companions. Finally, the author presents another hadith: 'Do not revile my Companions...' and explains the meaning of 'sarf' and 'adl' (obligatory and supererogatory acts, or vice versa), noting that the severe punishment is for one who deems reviling lawful or is a hyperbolic deterrent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That 'envy' in the text means the sin of wishing for removal of blessings, and that it is permissible to criticize the Companions as long as one does not curse them.
Correction: In this context, 'envy' refers to any harm or reviling of the Companions, which is strictly forbidden. Even criticism that leads to insult is prohibited.

Checkpoint
What does the hadith 'Do not revile my Companions...' say about their punishment?
A) They will be forgiven if they repent
B) They incur the curse of Allah, angels, and people
C) They will be punished only in the afterlife
D) They are simply rebuked

Key Takeaway
Harming or reviling the Companions is a grave sin, equated with harming the Prophet and Allah, with severe punishment in this life and the next.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever allowed your tongue to disparage a Companion, even in private, convinced that they were only human? How will you now guard your speech and thoughts, knowing that the Prophet equated harming them to harming himself?
?
When you hear debates about conflicts among the Sahaba, does your heart lean with envy or partisanship? Will you now choose to remain silent and avoid that disease, even when your emotions are stirred?
?
The Prophet adjured by Allah to not take his Companions as targets. Are there people in your life whom you target with your words, even subtly? How can you apply this lesson of reverence to all believers, beginning with the Companions?

The Three Guides of the Ummah
Conclusion synthesizing the three categories of guides: Malik (fiqh), Ash'ari (usul), Junayd (tasawwuf).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three categories of guides that lead the Muslim ummah in law, creed, and spirituality.

Core Idea
The ummah's guidance is threefold: fiqh, creed, and tasawwuf.

This concluding passage from the commentary synthesizes the entire discussion on the 'guides of the ummah.' It names the three representative figures—Imam Malik, Imam al-Ash'ari, and al-Junayd—each heading a vital domain of religious knowledge. Understanding this tripartite division helps you see how Sunni orthodoxy integrates jurisprudence, theology, and spiritual purification.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once for its rhythm, then the full translation. Notice how the verse from Qur'an 3:110 supports the elevated status of this ummah.
The author uses a tripartite structure: 'Imam Malik... Imam al-Ash'ari... al-Junayd...'
2
Identify the three domains and their guides
Find the three domains: furu' (branches of fiqh), usul (principles/creed), and tasawwuf. Note which imam is assigned to each.
3
Understand the hierarchy
The passage says these guides are 'the best of the best' after the Companions. Reflect on how this establishes a chain of authority.
4
Connect to your own learning
Ask yourself: why are all three fields necessary for a complete Islamic education? How do they complement each other?
The prayer at the end shows gratitude for all three.

وقوله : (هُدَاةُ الأُمَّهُ) أي: هداة هذه الأمة التي هي خير الأمم بشهادة قوله تعالى : كُنتُمْ خَيْرَ أُمَّةٍ أُخْرِجَتْ لِلنَّاسِ [آل عمران : ١١٠] فهم خيار الخيار، لكن بعد من ذكر من الصحابة ومن معهم .
والحاصل أن الإمام مالكاً ونحوه هداة الأمة في الفروع، والإمام الأشعري ونحوه هداة الأمة في الأصول ؛ أي: العقائد الدينية والجنيد ونحوه هداة الأمة في التصوف، فجزاهم الله عنا خيراً ونفعنا بهم .
And His saying: 'the guides of the ummah' i.e., the guides of this ummah which is the best of all nations as testified by His saying: 'You are the best of nations brought forth for mankind' (Al 'Imran 3:110). So they are the best of the best, but after those mentioned from the Companions and those with them.
The conclusion is that Imam Malik and his likes are the guides of the ummah in branches (furu'), Imam al-Ash'ari and his likes are the guides of the ummah in principles (usul), i.e., religious creeds, and al-Junayd and his likes are the guides of the ummah in Sufism. May Allah reward them all with good and benefit us through them.
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage is the concluding synthesis of the discussion on 'hudāt al-ummah'. It first identifies the ummah as the best of nations based on Quran 3:110. Then it categorizes the guides into three types: in the branches of fiqh, represented by Imam Malik and his ilk; in the principles of faith (usul al-din), represented by Imam al-Ash'ari and his followers; and in Sufism, represented by al-Junayd and his followers. This tripartite division establishes a comprehensive view of Sunni leadership across law, creed, and spirituality. The passage ends with a prayer for them.

Correction: The author explicitly includes creedal and spiritual guides as essential to the ummah's guidance.

Key Takeaway
The ummah's guidance is threefold: fiqh (Malik), creed (Ash'ari), and spirituality (Junayd), together forming a complete Sunni orthodoxy.

The Obligation of Taqlid for Non-Mujtahids
Commentary on line 82 states the obligation of taqlid with Quranic evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why taqlid (following a qualified scholar) is obligatory for those who cannot perform independent ijtihad, based on Quranic evidence.

Core Idea
Taqlid is not optional for the non-mujtahid—it is a Quranic command.

The poem states that taqlid of one of the four imams is obligatory. The commentary explains that since not everyone can perform absolute ijtihad, those lacking such qualification must follow an imam. The Quranic verse 'Ask the people of remembrance if you do not know' (al-Nahl 16:43) is cited as the primary evidence. In this lesson, we will unpack this argument and address a common misunderstanding about taqlid.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the poem line and its commentary once to get the overall meaning. Notice how the commentator builds the argument.
The line is part of the matn; the commentary expands on it.
2
Identify the Quranic evidence
Locate the verse cited and understand how it is used to justify taqlid. Ask yourself: what logical step connects the verse to the obligation?
The verse commands asking experts, which implies accepting their answer—that is taqlid.
3
Consider the dissenting view
The passage mentions that some scholars do not require taqlid of a specific imam. Note the nuance: the obligation is to follow a qualified scholar, not necessarily one fixed imam.
4
Reflect on the implications
Think about why this ruling matters for Islamic practice today. How does it preserve correct understanding of religion?
This demonstrates the importance of scholarly authority.

The prophecies
82 - So obligatory is taqlid of a scholar from them, thus the people narrated with wording that is understood.
His statement: 'So obligatory is taqlid... etc.' When he had established that the aforementioned imams are guides of this ummah, and not every person is capable of absolute ijtihad, he mentions here that it is obligatory upon everyone who does not possess the qualification for absolute ijtihad, even if he is a mujtahid of a school or a fatwa, to follow (taqlid) an imam from the four imams in the subsidiary rulings. And what the poet affirmed is the position of the usuliyyun and the majority of jurists and hadith scholars, and they adduce His statement: 'We ask the people of remembrance if you do not know' [al-Nahl 16:43]. So questioning is obligatory upon the one who does not know, and this entails accepting the statement of the scholar, and that is taqlid of him (1). And some said: it is not obligatory to follow one specific imam, but he may take (from whichever).
(1) The scholar Shaykh Muhammad 'Illish al-Maliki said in 'Fath al-'Ali al-Malik' (1/89) regarding a legal opinion sought from him on taqlid and matters of disagreement: 'Praise be to Allah, and prayers and peace be upon our master Muhammad, the Messenger of Allah: It is not permissible for a layperson to abandon taqlid of the four imams and take rulings from the Quran and hadith, because that has many conditions explained in usul that are not found in most scholars, especially in the latter times when Islam has become a stranger as it began a stranger, and because much of the Quran and hadith, its outward is clear disbelief, and its interpretation is not known except by Allah and those firmly grounded in knowledge.' Ibn 'Uyaynah said: 'The hadith is a misguidance except for the jurists'; he intended that others may take things at face value while it has an interpretation from another hadith, or a proof hidden from him, or an abrogated ruling necessitating its abandonment, along with other things that only one who has vast knowledge and deep understanding can handle. Malik said: 'Things become corrupted only when one removes them from their proper stations, and this dialectic is not part of the religion at all' – narrated by Ibn Yunus. In al-Bayan wa al-Tahsil: Malik said: 'The knowledge that is knowledge is the knowledge of the sunan and the established past practice that is known and acted upon.' 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Mahdi said: 'The earlier sunna from the practice of the people of Madina is better than the hadith.' Some of the Tabi'un would receive hadith from others and say: 'We do not deny this, but the practice has been on something else.' Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr ibn Jarir would sometimes be asked by his brother: 'Why did you not judge by such-and-such hadith?' He would say: 'I did not find the people upon it.' Al-Nakha'i said: 'If I had seen the Companions performing wudu up to the wrists, I would have done so, even though I read: to the elbows' [al-Ma'ida 5:6], because they are not accused of abandoning sunnas and they are the masters of knowledge. =
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on line 82 of the poem 'Jawharat al-Tawhid'. The line states that taqlid (following) of a scholar (ḥabr) from the four imams is obligatory. The commentary explains that since the imams are guides but not everyone can perform absolute ijtihad, it becomes obligatory for those lacking such qualification – even if they are mujtahids within a school or for issuing fatwas – to follow one of the four imams in subsidiary rulings. The commentator asserts that this is the position of the usul scholars, the majority of jurists, and hadith scholars, and they cite the Quranic verse 'So ask the people of remembrance if you do not know' (al-Nahl 16:43), which obligates questioning and consequently accepting the scholar's answer, i.e., taqlid. A dissenting view is mentioned that taqlid of a specific imam is not required; rather, one may take from any scholar. The lengthy footnote quotes Shaykh Muhammad 'Illish al-Maliki strongly warning against a layperson abandoning taqlid of the four imams and directly using Quran and hadith, citing the difficulty of conditions for ijtihad and the danger of misinterpretation. Additional quotes from Ibn 'Uyaynah, Malik, and others emphasize the importance of following established practice (amr māḍī) and the practice of the Madinese, and that hadith must be understood through the lens of the jurists and the consensus of the community.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Taqlid is blind following without evidence and is discouraged in Islam.
Correction: Taqlid for the non-mujtahid is an obligation commanded by the Quran (16:43) and upheld by the majority of scholars. It is not blind following but reliance on expert knowledge.

Obligation of Taqlid of a Four-Imam Scholar
Laqani states the obligation of taqlid and cites Quranic evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that taqlid of one of the four imams is obligatory for those lacking absolute ijtihad ability, and the Quranic evidence for this.

Core Idea
Taqlid is not optional for most Muslims; it's an obligation based on a Quranic command.

In this passage, al-Laqani establishes the duty of taqlid for those who cannot reach the level of absolute ijtihad. The commentator explains the reasoning and provides the primary scriptural proof from Surah al-Nahl. We'll also encounter a minority view that permits switching between schools.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation to get an overview of the content.
Pay attention to the key terms like taqlid and ijtihad.
2
Identify the two positions
Notice that the passage first states the obligation of taqlid, then presents a minority view that rejects restriction to one imam.
3
Understand the Quranic evidence
The verse 'Ask the people of remembrance' (16:43) is used as the primary proof. Reflect on how this implies accepting the scholar's statement.
4
Understand the scope
Taqlid is obligatory only for those not qualified for absolute ijtihad. Even a mujtahid within a school must follow a school.

فَواجِبٌ تَقْلِيدُ حَبْرٍ مِنْهُمُ كَذَا حَكَى القومُ بِلَفْظ يُفْهَمُ قوله : (فَواجِبٌ تَقْلِيدُ ... إلخ) لما قدَّم أن الأئمة المذكورين هداة هذه الأمة، ولم يكن كل واحد من الناس قادراً على الاجتهاد المطلق، ذكر هنا أنه يجب على كل من لم يكن فيه أهلية الاجتهاد المطلق، ولو كان مجتهد مذهب أو فتوى تقليد إمام من الأئمة الأربعة في الأحكام الفرعية وما جزم به الناظم هو مذهب الأصوليين وجمهور الفقهاء والمحدثين واحتجوا بقوله تعالى: ﴿فَاسْأَلُوا أَهْلَ الذِّكْرِ إِن كُنتُمْ لَا تَعْلَمُونَ﴾ [النحل : ٤٣] فأوجب السؤال على من لم يعلم، ويترتب عليه الأخذ بقول العالم، وذلك تقليد له، وقال بعضهم : لا يجب تقليد واحد بعينه، بل له أن يأخذ فيما يقع له بهذا المذهب تارة وبغيره أخرى، فيجوز صلاة الظهر على مذهب الإمام الشافعي، وصلاة العصر على مذهب مالك، وهكذا.
So it is obligatory to follow (taqlid) a scholar (hibr) from among them. Thus the people narrated with a wording that is understood. His statement: 'So it is obligatory to follow... etc.': Since he had presented that the aforementioned imams are the guides of this nation, and not every person is capable of absolute ijtihad, he mentioned here that it is obligatory upon everyone who does not possess the qualification for absolute ijtihad – even if he is a mujtahid of a school or a fatwa – to follow (taqlid) one of the four imams in subsidiary rulings (al-ahkam al-far'iyya). What the author has affirmed is the position of the usuliyyun and the majority of jurists and hadith scholars. They argued with the saying of Allah the Exalted: 'Ask the people of remembrance if you do not know' (Qur'an 16:43). Thus He made it obligatory to ask for one who does not know, and upon that follows taking the statement of the knowledgeable person, and that is taqlid of him. And some said: It is not obligatory to follow (taqlid) one specific person, rather he may take in what occurs to him from this school sometimes and from another at other times, so afternoon prayer according to the school of al-Shafi'i and 'asr prayer according to the school of Malik is permissible, and so on.
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage defines the obligation of taqlid of one of the four imams for those not qualified for absolute ijtihad. The author (al-Laqani in the poem) states that taqlid of a scholar (hibr) from among them is obligatory. The commentator explains that since the imams were introduced as guides, and not everyone can be a mujtahid, taqlid is obligatory for those without absolute ijtihad ability, even if they are mujtahids within a school or fatwa (i.e., limited ijtihad). The evidence is from Qur'an 16:43, which commands asking the people of remembrance, implying acceptance of their statement (taqlid). The passage then presents an alternative view: some say taqlid is not restricted to one specific imam; one can follow different imams for different issues, e.g., Shafi'i for zuhr and Maliki for 'asr. Thus the lesson establishes the main position and acknowledges a minority view.

Conditions and Scope of Taqlid Among the Four Imams
Commentary clarifies taqlid conditions and limits to four imams.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand who is obligated to perform taqlid, why it is limited to the four imams, and the exception for personal practice.

Core Idea
Taqlid is only for those lacking ijtihad, and only from codified schools.

This passage from Tuhfat al-Murid clarifies the practical rules of taqlid. It explains that taqlid is forbidden for those with ijtihad ability, and that followers must adhere to one of the four imams whose schools are systematically recorded. However, it also notes a permission to follow other scholars in non-fatwa matters.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the three main points: the ruling for mujtahids, the limitation to four imams, and the exception for personal practice.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify who is obligated and who is forbidden from taqlid
The passage states that taqlid is forbidden for those with absolute ijtihad ability. For others, it is obligatory. Find the wording that makes this distinction.
Look for the phrase 'haram' and 'obligation'.
3
Understand why only four imams
The passage explains that taqlid is restricted to the four imams because their schools were recorded and codified. Other scholars, even senior companions, cannot be followed in fatwa because their views were not systematically preserved.
4
Note the exception for non-fatwa matters
The passage quotes the verse allowing taqlid of other than the four in matters other than giving fatwa. This means personal practice may follow other scholars, but official fatwa must be from the four.
This exception shows some flexibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وخرج بقولنا : مَنْ لم يكن فيه أهلية الاجتهاد المطلق من كان فيه أهليته، فإنه يحرم عليه التقليد فيما يقع له عند الأكثر ، واختاره الآمدي وابن الحاجب والسبكي من الاجتهاد الذي هو أصل التقليد، وأما التقليد في العقائد فقد علمته في صدر هذه المنظومة وقوله : (حَبْرٍ مِنْهُمُ) بفتح الحاء وكسرها ; أي: عالم حاذق من الأئمة الأربعة، ولا يجوز تقليد غيرهم، ولو كان من أكابر الصحابة؛ لأن مذاهبهم لم تدون، ولم تضبط كمذاهب هؤلاء، لكن جوز بعضهم ذلك في غير الإفتاء كما قال : وجائِزٌ تَقْلِيدُ غَيْرِ الأَرْبَعَهُ فِي غَيْرِ إِفْتاء وفِي هَذَا سَعَهُ وقوله : كَذَا حَتَّى القَوْمُ بِلَفْظِ يُفْهَمُ) أي: حكى الأصوليون وجمهور الفقهاء والمحدثين بلفظ يفهمه السامع لوضوحه حكماً مثل هذا الحكم الذي هو وجوب تقليد إمام من الأئمة الأربعة، واختلف المشبه والمشبه به بالاعتبار، فإن القول باعتبار كونه صادراً من المصنف غير نفسه باعتبار كونه صادراً من القوم، وليس مراد المتن التبري من ذلك، بل مجرد العَزْمِ.
And he excluded by our saying: 'one who does not have the qualification for absolute ijtihad' – one who has that qualification, then taqlid is forbidden for him in what occurs to him according to the majority, and it was chosen by al-Amidi, Ibn al-Hajib, and al-Subki from the ijtihad that is the basis of taqlid. As for taqlid in beliefs (al-'aqa'id), you have learned it in the beginning of this poem. And his statement: 'a scholar (hibr) from among them' – with fat-h of the ha' and kasr, meaning a proficient scholar from the four imams. It is not permissible to follow (taqlid) others, even if they are from the senior companions, because their schools were not recorded and were not codified like the schools of these. However, some permitted that in other than giving fatwa, as he said: 'And it is permissible to follow other than the four in other than giving fatwa, and in this there is ample scope.' And his statement: 'thus the people narrated with a wording that is understood' – i.e., the usuliyyun and the majority of jurists and hadith scholars narrated with a wording that the listener understands due to its clarity a ruling similar to this ruling which is the obligation of following an imam from the four imams. The comparison (tashbih) and the compared (mushabbah bihi) differ by consideration: for the statement is considered as emanating from the author not himself, as it is considered as emanating from the people. The intended meaning of the text is not disassociation from that, but mere determination.
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage clarifies the conditions and scope of taqlid. First, the commentator explains that the obligation of taqlid applies only to those lacking absolute ijtihad ability. For those who have ijtihad ability, taqlid is forbidden (haram) according to the majority, including al-Amidi, Ibn al-Hajib, and al-Subki. The commentator reminds that taqlid in creed is a separate matter already covered. Second, the phrase 'scholar from among them' is explained: it refers specifically to one of the four imams; taqlid of others, even senior companions, is not allowed because their schools were not systematically recorded and codified like the four. However, some scholars permitted following other than the four in non-fatwa matters (i.e., personal practice) as indicated by the verse 'it is permissible to follow other than the four in other than giving fatwa'. Third, the phrase 'thus the people narrated with a wording that is understood' is explained: the usuliyyun and majority narrated a clear ruling analogous to this one. The comparison in the text considers the ruling as emanating from the author not himself, but as a report from the people. The author's intent is not to disclaim the ruling but simply to assert it.

Key Terms
أهلية الاجتهاد
تقليد في العقائد
تدوين
الإفتاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think any scholar's opinion can be followed in all matters.
Correction: The passage restricts taqlid to the four imams because their schools are codified, except for non-fatwa matters where following others is allowed.

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on taqlid for a person who possesses absolute ijtihad ability?
A) It is obligatory
B) It is recommended
C) It is forbidden
D) It is permissible

Key Takeaway
Taqlid is only required for those without ijtihad, and only from the four codified madhhabs, with a leeway for personal practice from others.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever blindly followed a madhhab simply because of family tradition, without ever honestly assessing whether you personally lack the qualification for ijtihad? If you are not a mujtahid, are you willing to accept that you must follow one of the four codified schools, even when it feels restrictive? What step will you take today to ensure your practice is grounded in legitimate taqlid rather than mere custom?
?
The passage reminds us that taqlid in beliefs (aqeedah) is different and was covered earlier. Have you ever accepted a creedal statement—such as about Allah's attributes—without wrestling with the evidence from the Quran and Sunnah? Do you treat matters of faith with the same passive acceptance as you do fiqh rulings, or do you actively seek certainty? What one belief will you resolve to investigate more deeply this week?
?
Consider the ease with which we often turn to popular contemporary scholars or internet fatwas instead of the four madhhabs. Does your heart prefer convenience over the disciplined structure of the codified schools? The passage allows following others only in personal practice, not in giving fatwa. Are you crossing that line by giving or following rulings outside the four schools without proper authorization? How can you realign your practice with this guidance?

Three Opinions on Transferring Between Legal Schools
Commentary presents three positions on changing one's madhhab affiliation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three classical positions on changing one's madhhab and the reasoning behind each.

Core Idea
Transferring between madhhabs is debated: prohibited, permitted, or conditional.

This short passage from the commentary addresses a practical question for followers of a madhhab: can one transfer to another school? The commentator presents three distinct opinions, ranging from absolute prohibition to conditional permission. Understanding these positions clarifies the boundaries of madhhab adherence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Let the structure of question and answer come through.
Notice the concise style: a question followed by 'three opinions'.
2
Identify the three opinions
List the three opinions as presented: (1) absolutely prohibited, (2) absolutely permissible, (3) permissible if one does not combine between two schools.
The third opinion includes a condition.
3
Understand the nuance of the third opinion
The third opinion is not blanket permission; it prohibits combining rulings from different schools in a way that leads to contradiction. This is a middle position preserving consistency.
This guards against the misconception that the third opinion allows incoherent mixing.
4
Reflect on why this matters
Think about how these opinions reflect different attitudes toward legal authority and consistency. This sets the stage for discussions on taqlid and ijtihad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قلت: هل يجوز الانتقال من مذهب إلى مذهب؟ قلت : فيه أقوال ثلاثة : فقيل : يمتنع مطلقاً، وقيل: يجوز مطلقاً ، وقيل : إن لم يجمع بين المذهبين
If you say: Is it permissible to transfer from one school (madhhab) to another? I say: There are three opinions: 1. It is absolutely prohibited. 2. It is absolutely permissible. 3. It is permissible if he does not combine between the two schools.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage addresses a practical question: can a person transfer from one madhhab to another? The commentator presents three opinions: (1) absolute prohibition, likely because it undermines consistency and authority; (2) absolute permissibility, allowing freedom to choose any school; (3) conditional permissibility: allowed as long as one does not combine rulings from different schools in a contradictory manner. The third position seeks a middle ground, allowing flexibility while avoiding internal contradiction. The passage is brief but captures the key differences.

Key Terms
انتقال
مذهب
أقوال ثلاثة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the third opinion gives blanket permission to transfer without any condition.
Correction: The third opinion explicitly prohibits combining schools in a contradictory manner; it requires that one not mix rulings from different schools in a single issue.

Checkpoint
According to the third opinion, when is transferring between madhhabs permissible?
A) Always
B) Never
C) If one does not combine between the two schools
D) Only with approval of a scholar

Key Takeaway
The third opinion allows transferring between madhhabs so long as one does not combine rulings from different schools in a contradictory manner.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you find a ruling from a different school more convenient than your own, do you immediately adopt it without considering whether you are truly transferring or simply combining? What does your current practice reveal about your sincerity in following a madhhab?
?
Have you ever dismissed the first opinion (absolute prohibition) as too strict without understanding its rationale of preserving methodological integrity? How might your respect for scholarly discipline grow if you took that view seriously?
?
If you had to defend the consistency of your religious practice before Allah, could you honestly say you have not combined rulings from different schools merely for personal ease? What concrete step will you take to ensure your practice aligns with one consistent methodology?

The Obligation of Taqlid and Restriction to the Four Imams
Definition of taqlid for non-mujtahid and restriction to four imams.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that taqlid is obligatory for those who lack the capacity for ijtihad and must be limited to the four well-recorded imams, with a limited exception.

Core Idea
Taqlid is a duty for non-mujtahid, anchored in the four imams' preserved schools.

This passage from 'Tuhfat al-Mureed' clarifies the ruling of taqlid—following a qualified scholar—for those who cannot perform ijtihad. While taqlid becomes obligatory for such individuals, the author emphasizes that valid taqlid is restricted to the four renowned imams, whose schools were meticulously recorded and transmitted. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this restriction and the minor exception for non-fatwa matters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on taqlid
Read the first part of the passage to understand who is obligated to perform taqlid and who is forbidden from it. Note the discussion of ijtihad capacity.
The author specifies that taqlid is forbidden for a mujtahid but obligatory for others.
2
Understand the restriction to the four imams
Focus on the explanation of 'حَبْرٍ مِنْهُمُ' (a learned scholar from them). See why only the four imams' schools are considered valid for following, and why even great Companions are excluded.
3
Examine the exception
Look at the part about 'في غير الإفتاء' (other than issuing fatwas). The author allows following other scholars in non-fatwa contexts, providing a narrow flexibility.
This shows that the restriction is not absolute.
4
Reflect on the transmission of the ruling
The passage ends by noting that scholars (uṣūliyyūn, jurists, hadith scholars) transmitted this ruling clearly. Consider why such transmission matters for authority.
This underscores the consensus behind the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وخرج بقولنا : مَنْ لم يكن فيه أهلية الاجتهاد (المطلق من كان فيه أهليته، فإنه يحرم عليه التقليد فيما يقع له عند الأكثر ، واختاره الآمدي وابن الحاجب والسبكي من الاجتهاد الذي هو أصل التقليد، وأما التقليد في العقائد فقد علمته في صدر هذه المنظومة (١) وقوله : (حَبْرٍ مِنْهُمُ) بفتح الحاء وكسرها ؛ أي: عالم حاذق من الأئمة الأربعة، ولا يجوز تقليد غيرهم، ولو كان من أكابر الصحابة؛ لأن مذاهبهم لم تدون، ولم تضبط كمذاهب هؤلاء، لكن جوز بعضهم ذلك في غير الإفتاء كما قال : وجائِزٌ تَقْلِيدُ غَيْرِ الأَرْبَعَهُ فِي غَيْرِ إِفْتاء وفِي هَذَا سَعَهُ وقوله : كَذَا حَتَّى القَوْمُ بِلَفْظِ يُفْهَمُ) أي: حكى الأصوليون وجمهور الفقهاء والمحدثين بلفظ يفهمه السامع لوضوحه حكماً مثل هذا الحكم الذي هو وجوب تقليد إمام من الأئمة الأربعة، واختلف المشبه والمشبه به بالاعتبار، فإن القول باعتبار كونه صادراً من المصنف غير نفسه باعتبار كونه صادراً من القوم، وليس مراد المتن التبري من ذلك، بل مجرد العَزْمِ.
And He said: 'مَنْ لم يكن فيه أهلية الاجتهاد' (absolute who has its qualification), for taqlid is forbidden for him regarding what occurs to him according to the majority, and al-Amidi, Ibn al-Hajib, and al-Subki chose it from the ijtihad which is the foundation of taqlid. As for taqlid in beliefs, you have known it in the beginning of this poem. And His saying: 'حَبْرٍ مِنْهُمُ' with fatḥa and kasra of the ḥā; meaning: a skilled scholar from the four imams, and it is not permissible to follow others, even if they are from the great Companions, because their schools were not recorded nor preserved like the schools of these. However, some permitted that in other than issuing fatwas, as he said: 'And permissible is following other than the four in other than issuing fatwas, and in this there is broadness.' And His saying: 'كَذَا حَتَّى القَوْمُ بِلَفْظِ يُفْهَمُ' meaning: the uṣūliyyūn and the majority of jurists and hadith scholars narrated with a wording that the listener understands due to its clarity a ruling like this ruling which is the obligation of following an imam from the four imams. And the comparison and the compared differ by consideration, for the statement that it is issued from the author other than himself is considered issued from the people, and the intention of the text is not self-exculpation from that, but merely determination.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage defines the ruling of taqlid for one who lacks the qualification for ijtihad (absolute or affiliated). The author states that the majority hold that such a person is forbidden from doing taqlid in matters that arise for him, and he attributes this view to al-Amidi, Ibn al-Hajib, and al-Subki. Then the author explains the phrase 'حَبْرٍ مِنْهُمُ' (a learned scholar from them) from the poem, clarifying that it refers to a skilled scholar from the four imams. He asserts that it is not permissible to follow imams other than the four, even if they are from the great Companions, because their schools were not documented and preserved like the schools of the four. However, some scholars have permitted following others in matters that do not involve issuing fatwas, quoting a line of poetry: 'Permissible is following other than the four in issuing rulings other than fatwas, and in this there is broadness.' The author then explains the phrase 'كَذَا حَتَّى القَوْمُ بِلَفْظِ يُفْهَمُ' (similarly, even the people with a wording that is understood), stating that the uṣūliyyūn, jurists, and hadith scholars have transmitted a clear ruling similar to this ruling—the obligation of following one of the four imams. He notes the difference between the likened and the likened according to consideration: the statement that it is from the author is not considered as from the people, but the intention is not self-exculpation, just determination of the ruling.

Key Terms
تقليد
اجتهاد
أئمة أربعة
حبر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think taqlid is always forbidden for everyone.
Correction: The passage clarifies that taqlid is obligatory for those who lack ijtihad, and only forbidden for mujtahids.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why is it not permissible to follow imams other than the four even if they are from the great Companions?
A) Because their schools are not transmitted reliably
B) Because the Companions were not qualified
C) Because the four imams are infallible
D) Because following others is forbidden in all cases

Key Takeaway
Taqlid for non-mujtahid is a binding duty, and valid taqlid is confined to the four imams due to the preservation of their schools, with a narrow exception for non-fatwa contexts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you practice your religion, do you consciously follow a specific madhhab with knowledge of its foundations, or do you mix opinions based on convenience? This passage demands accountability in how you learn and apply fiqh. What concrete step will you take this week to commit to a preserved school?
?
The passage says taqlid is obligatory for non-mujtahid. Are you a mujtahid? If not, have you accepted your need to follow qualified scholars, or do you rely on your own reasoning in matters you have not studied? What scares you more: being dependent on scholars or being wrong about Allah's command?
?
Consider the exception for non-fatwa contexts: you may advise or teach others. Do you always ensure your guidance is rooted in the reliable transmission of the four imams? When was the last time you gave a religious opinion without verifying its source? How will you change your practice starting today?

The Three Opinions on Changing Madhhabs
The author answers a question about changing madhhabs, presenting three opinions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three scholarly opinions regarding transferring from one madhhab to another, especially the conditional prohibition.

Core Idea
Changing madhhabs is not a free-for-all; it has conditions.

Before exploring the detailed rulings on following a madhhab, a common question arises: can one switch between madhhabs freely? The author presents three opinions from the scholars, including a nuanced middle position. This lesson introduces those opinions and sets the stage for understanding the proper attitude towards the imams.

Guided Path
1
Read the question and three answers
Read the Arabic passage and translation carefully. Notice the structure: a question followed by three opinions.
The third opinion includes a condition.
2
Identify the condition in the third opinion
The third opinion prohibits transferring only if one combines rulings in a way no scholar holds. Reflect on why this is problematic.
This prevents picking and choosing for convenience.
3
Consider the praise of the imams
The author adds that the imams were most eager to follow the Prophet, and anyone who thinks otherwise is suspect. Why is this important?
It shows respect for the founders of the schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قلت: هل يجوز الانتقال من مذهب إلى مذهب؟ قلت : فيه أقوال ثلاثة : فقيل : يمتنع مطلقاً، وقيل: يجوز مطلقاً ، وقيل : إن لم يجمع بين المذهبين وأحرص خلْقِ الله على اتباع رسول الله ، ولا يظن ذلك بهم أحد إلا ذو ريبة في دينه . وقد بني مالك رضي الله تعالى عنه مذهبه على أربعة أشياء: الأول: آية قرآنية، والثاني: حديث صحيح سالم من المعارضة، الثالث: إجماع أهل المدينة، الرابع: اتفاق جمهورهم. وقد أجمع أهل السنة على وجوب التقليد على من ليس فيه أهلية الاجتهاد حسب ما في «الديباج» للإمام ابن فرحون رحمه الله تعالى، وعمدة المريد للشيخ اللقاني وغيرهما، وشاع ذلك حتى صار معلوماً من الدين بالضرورة).
If you say: Is it permissible to transfer from one school to another? I say: Concerning it are three sayings: It was said: It is prohibited absolutely, and it was said: It is permissible absolutely, and it was said: If he does not combine between the two schools. And the most eager of Allah's creation to follow the Messenger of Allah, and no one would think that of them except one with doubt in his religion. And Malik, may Allah be pleased with him, built his school on four things: First: a Qur'anic verse, Second: an authentic hadith free from opposition, Third: the consensus of the people of Medina, Fourth: the agreement of their majority. And Ahl al-Sunnah have agreed upon the obligation of taqlid for one who does not have the qualification for ijtihad, according to what is in 'al-Dibāj' by Imam Ibn Farhoun, may Allah have mercy on him, and 'Umdat al-Murīd' by Shaykh al-Laqānī and others, and this became widespread until it became known from the religion by necessity.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage deals with an objection: Is it permissible to transfer from one madhhab to another? The author presents three opinions: (1) absolute prohibition, (2) absolute permission, and (3) conditional prohibition—if he does not combine between two schools in a way that no scholar holds. In the third opinion, if he combines rulings in a way that produces a ruling contrary to consensus, it is prohibited. The author then extols the imams as most eager to follow the Prophet, warning that anyone who thinks otherwise has doubt in his religion. He then describes how Imam Malik built his school on four foundations: the Quran, authentic hadith free from opposition, the consensus of the people of Medina, and the agreement of their majority—illustrating the reliability of the four schools. The passage concludes with a statement of consensus among Ahl al-Sunnah on the obligation of taqlid for those lacking ijtihad, citing two works, and asserts that this is known from the religion by necessity.

Misconception: Some think transferring between madhhabs is always allowed without restriction.
Correction: The third opinion shows it is prohibited if one combines schools in a way that produces a ruling not held by any scholar.

Checkpoint

A) When it is done frequently
B) When it combines rulings in a way no scholar holds
C) When it is for a worldly benefit
D) When it is from a less strict to a stricter school

Key Takeaway
Transferring madhhabs is subject to conditions; arbitrary combination leading to unprecedented rulings is prohibited.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

The Four Foundations of the Maliki School
The author describes the four sources of the Maliki school as evidence of its authenticity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four sources upon which Imam Malik built his school and why they ensure reliability.

Core Idea
A madhhab is built on solid textual foundations, not personal opinion.

To counter the notion that following a madhhab is blind imitation, the author briefly describes how Imam Malik constructed his school on four clear principles. This shows that the schools are grounded in authentic sources. This lesson explores those four foundations.

These are the primary sources for Maliki fiqh.

The consensus and agreement of Madinans is unique to Maliki school.
3
Reflect on implications
Why did the author include this detail? It shows the schools are not arbitrary but based on evidence.
This reinforces the obligation of taqlid for non-mujtahids.
