The Three Conditions for Obligation and the Scholarly Disagreement
Author enumerates three conditions and presents a scholarly dispute on the third.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three conditions that trigger the obligation and the different scholarly views on whether expectation of efficacy is required.

Core Idea
The obligation depends on knowledge, safety from greater harm, and—according to some—a prospect of effect.

While the duty to enjoin good and forbid evil is established, its actual obligation is conditional. Scholars debate whether one must have knowledge, avoid causing greater harm, and expect a positive outcome. This lesson examines these conditions and a key disagreement over the requirement of anticipated efficacy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on conditions
Read the Arabic passage and translation carefully. Note the three conditions listed and the subsequent discussion.
The conditions are introduced with 'واعلم أن لوجوب الأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر شروطاً'.
2
Identify and understand the three conditions
List each condition: knowledge, safety from greater evil, and expectation of efficacy. Understand what each entails.
The first two conditions are agreed upon; the third is disputed.
3
Analyze the scholarly disagreement
Compare the views of al-Qarafi, al-Sa'd/al-Amidi, and the majority (Shafi'is). Note the differing rulings: obligation, permissibility, or continued obligation.
The majority hold that the duty remains even if no effect is expected.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الإجماعُ فلأن المسلمين في الصدر الأول وبعده كانوا يتواصون بذلك، ويوبخون تاركه مع الاقتدار عليه ولا يشكل على وجوب الأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر قوله تعالى: ﴿يَأَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا عَلَيْكُمْ أَنفُسَكُمْ لَا يَضُرُكُم مِّن ضَلَّ إِذَا اهْتَدَيْتُهُ﴾ [المائدة: ١٠٥]؛ لأن المعنى إذا فعلتم ما كُلّفتم به ؛ ومنه الأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر .. لا يضركم فعل غيركم للمعصية، فصارت الآية دالة على وجوب الأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر، قال ابن مسعود : إن من أكبر الذنوب عند الله أن يُقال للعبد : اتق الله فيقول : عليك بنفسك). وفي الحديث : «مَنْ قيل له : اتق الله، فغضب وقفَ يوم القيامة، فلم يبقَ ملك إلا مرَّ به وقال له : أنت الذي قيل لك : اتق الله ، فغضبت»؛ يعني يوبخونه. واعلم أن لوجوب الأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر شروطاً : أحدها: أن يكون المتولي لذلك عالماً بما يأمر به وينهى عنه، فالجاهل بالحكم لا يحل له الأمر ولا النهي فليس للعوام أمر ولا نهي فيما يجهلونه؛ وأما الذي استوى في معرفته العام والخاص ففيه للعالم وغيره الأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر . كأن ينهي عن شرب الخمر وثانيها : أن يأمن أن يُؤدي إنكاره إلى منكرٍ أكبر منه ، فيؤدي نهيه عنه إلى قتل النفس أو نحوه فعدم هذين الشرطين يوجب التحريم . وثالثها : أن يغلب على ظنه أن أمره بالمعروف مُؤكِّرٌ في تحصيله، وأن تهيه عن المنكر مزيل له، وعدم هذا الشرط يُسقط الوجوب، ويبقي الجواز إذا قطع بعدم الإفادة، والندب إذا شك فيها . قاله القرافي وغيره. وقال السعد والآمدي بالوجوب فيما لو ظنَّ عدم الإفادة، أو شك فيها، بخلاف ما إذا قطع بعدم الإفادة. ولفظ السعد ومن الشروط تجويز التأثير بألا يعلم قطعاً عدم التأثير، لئلا يكون عبثاً واشتغالاً بما لا يعني انتهى. ونحوه قول الآمدي : من شروط الوجوب ألا ييأس من إجابته، انتهى. وقال أكثرُ العلماء كالشافعية : لا يشترط هذا الشرط ؛ لأن الذي عليه الأمر والنهي لا القبول، كما قال تعالى: ﴿مَا عَلَى الرَّسُولِ إِلَّا الْبَلَاعُ﴾ [المائدة: ٩٩]، وقال تعالى: ﴿وَذَكِّرْ فَإِنَّ الذِّكْرَى تَنفَعُ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ﴾ [الذاريات: ٥٥]؛ ولذلك قال النووي: قال العلماء: ولا يسقط عن المكلف الأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر ؛ لكونه لا يفيد في ظنه، بل يجب عليه فعله. انتهى ملخصاً من «شرح المصنف»، ومن حاشية الشنواني».
As for consensus, the Muslims in the early period and after used to enjoin one another to that, and rebuke the one who abandons it while able. And it is not problematic for the obligation of commanding good and forbidding evil the saying of the Exalted: 'O you who have believed, upon yourselves is [responsibility]. Those who have gone astray will not harm you when you have been guided' (Quran 5:105); because the meaning is: when you do what you are charged with—including commanding good and forbidding evil—the sin of others does not harm you. So the verse indicates the obligation of commanding good and forbidding evil. Ibn Mas'ud said: 'Among the greatest sins with Allah is that it is said to a servant: Fear Allah, and he replies: Mind yourself.' And in the hadith: 'Whoever is told: Fear Allah, and becomes angry, will stop on the Day of Resurrection, and no angel will pass by him except he says to him: You are the one who was told: Fear Allah, and you became angry'—meaning they rebuke him. And know that the obligation of commanding good and forbidding evil has conditions: One of them: that the one undertaking that be knowledgeable of what he commands and forbids; for the ignorant of the ruling is not permitted to command or forbid, so the common people have no command or forbidding in what they are ignorant of. As for that which is equally known to common and specific, both the scholar and others may command good and forbid evil—like forbidding drinking wine. The second: that he be secure that his forbidding will not lead to a greater evil, such as his forbidding leading to killing of a soul or the like; the absence of these two conditions necessitates prohibition. The third: that he be predominantly certain that his commanding good will be effective in attaining it, and his forbidding evil will remove it; the absence of this condition removes obligation, and leaves permissibility if he is certain of lack of benefit, and recommendation if he doubts it. Al-Qarafi and others said this. Al-Sa'd and al-Amidi said obligation even if he thinks lack of benefit or doubts it, contrary to when he is certain of lack of benefit. Al-Sa'd's wording: 'Among the conditions is allowing for effect, such that he does not know for certain the lack of effect, to avoid futility and occupation with what does not concern him.' End quote. Similar is the saying of al-Amidi: 'Among the conditions of obligation is that he not despair of his response.' End quote. Most scholars, like the Shafi'is, said: this condition is not required, because the one who commands and forbids is only responsible for the command and prohibition, not acceptance, as the Exalted said: 'Not upon the Messenger is except conveyance' (Quran 5:99), and said: 'And remind, for indeed the reminder benefits the believers' (Quran 51:55). Therefore al-Nawawi said: The scholars said: It does not drop from the responsible person commanding good and forbidding evil due to his thinking it will not benefit; rather it is obligatory upon him. End quote, summarized from 'Sharh al-Musannaf' and from 'Hashiyat al-Shanwani'.
Source pages p. 406

Commentary
This passage discusses the basis and conditions for the obligation of commanding good and forbidding evil. The author begins by citing consensus (ijma') as evidence: early Muslims exhorted one another and rebuked those who neglected it. He then addresses a potential objection from Quran 5:105 ('Upon yourselves is your responsibility'), explaining that the verse means if you fulfill your duty—which includes commanding good and forbidding evil—the misguidance of others does not harm you, so the verse actually supports the obligation. He quotes a hadith warning against angrily rejecting admonition. The author then lists three conditions for obligation: (1) the person must have knowledge of what he commands and forbids; commoners may only act on matters equally known to all, like forbidding alcohol. (2) The forbidding must not lead to a greater evil (e.g., death); if it does, it becomes forbidden. (3) There must be a predominant expectation of efficacy; if one is certain of no effect, it becomes permissible (not obligatory), and if doubtful, recommended. The author notes a difference of opinion: al-Qarafi holds the condition of expected efficacy; al-Sa'd and al-Amidi hold that obligation remains even if one expects no effect, except when certain of no effect; but most scholars (e.g., Shafi'is) do not require this condition, citing verses that the duty is only to convey (Quran 5:99, 51:55), and al-Nawawi affirms that it remains obligatory regardless of apparent benefit.

Key Terms

الوجوب
الجواز
الندب
التأثير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If a person thinks their advice will not be accepted, the duty of commanding good and forbidding evil drops.
Correction: The majority of scholars hold that the duty remains even if one expects no effect, because the responsibility is to convey, not to ensure acceptance. The passage cites Quranic evidence for this.

Checkpoint
According to the majority opinion presented in the passage, what is the ruling on commanding good and forbidding evil when one is certain that it will have no effect?
A) It becomes forbidden.
B) It becomes permissible but not obligatory.
C) It remains obligatory.
D) It is recommended.

Key Takeaway
The obligation of commanding good and forbidding evil is conditional on knowledge and safety from greater harm, but the requirement of expected efficacy is disputed; the majority hold that the duty remains regardless.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When was the last time you remained silent about a wrong because you were afraid of a negative reaction? Based on this lesson, does your fear outweigh the obligation to speak? What will you do next time?
?
If you knew that your advice would be rejected and even mocked, would you still have the courage to give it for the sake of Allah? Are you ready to be like the Messenger who only had to convey?
?
Consider a situation where forbidding an evil might lead to a greater evil. How will you determine that balance in your own life? Are you truly weighing harms objectively, or are you using fear as an excuse to avoid responsibility?

The Blameworthy Argumentation: Definition and Prohibition
Defines argumentation and states its blameworthy uses with hadith evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of mira' and why it is blameworthy when done to belittle others.

Core Idea
Not all argumentation is bad; it's blameworthy only when aimed at superiority.

In this lesson, we explore the concept of argumentation (mira') as defined by Imam Sanusi, distinguishing its blameworthy form from its commendable counterpart. The source passage draws on linguistic roots and prophetic warnings to highlight the dangers of excessive disputation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on definition
Read the Arabic and translation of the definition of mira' (linguistic and technical). Notice the root meaning 'extraction'.
The technical definition involves disputing someone's claim of correctness.
2
Identify the blameworthy condition
Find the phrase that states when mira' is blameworthy. What intention makes it forbidden?
It's when the goal is to belittle the opponent and show superiority.
3
Examine the hadith warnings
Read the two hadiths: one about 'nitpickers' (mutanatti'un) and another about those who make scholars err with difficult questions. What do they teach?
These hadiths reinforce the prohibition of harmful argumentation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وَكَالمِرَاء) هو لغةٌ : الاستخراج يقال مارى فلان فلاناً، إذا استخرج ما عنده، وعر فاً : منازعة الغير فيما يدعي صوابه ، ومحل كونه مذموماً إذا كان لتحقير غيرك، وإظهار مزيتك عليه . وقد ورد في الحديث: «هلك المتنطعونَ ... ثلاثاً; أي: المتعمقون في البحث . وأخرج الطبراني عن ثوبان مرفوعاً: سيكون في أمتي أقوامٌ يُغَلِّطُون فقهاءَهم بعُضَل المسائل - بضم العين وفتح الضاد; أي صعابها - أولئك شرارُ أمتي ، وأما إذا كان لإحقاق حق، وإبطال باطل ; أي: لإظهار حقية الحق، وإظهار بطلان الباطل، فممدوح شرعاً ولو من ولد لوالده; فيكون عقوقاً محموداً.
His statement: (and like argumentation) is linguistically: extraction; one says 'he argued with so-and-so' when he extracts what he has, and technically: disputing with another regarding what he claims to be correct. And the place of its being blameworthy is when it is to belittle your opponent and show your superiority over him. And it has been reported in the hadith: 'Destroyed are the nitpickers' ... three times; i.e., those who delve deeply into research. And al-Tabarani reported from Thawban as a marfu' hadith: 'There will be in my nation people who will make their scholars err with difficult questions - with damma on 'ayn and fatha on dad, i.e., their difficult ones - those are the worst of my nation.' But if it is for the establishment of truth and the nullification of falsehood; i.e., to manifest the truthfulness of truth and the falsehood of falsehood, then it is commendable religiously, even if from a child to his parent; thus it would be a praiseworthy disobedience.
Source pages p. 416

Commentary
This passage defines mira' (argumentation/disputation) both linguistically and technically, then distinguishes between its blameworthy and commendable forms. Linguistically, it derives from 'extraction'. Technically, it is disputing with someone about what they claim to be correct. The blameworthy form occurs when the intent is to belittle the opponent and demonstrate superiority. The author supports this with hadith warnings against excessive nitpicking and making scholars err with difficult questions. However, if the argumentation aims to establish truth and refute falsehood, it becomes praiseworthy and even an act of worship, to the extent that it overrides filial obedience—a child may respectfully correct his parent in such a case.

Key Terms
المراء
المتنطعون
العضل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All forms of argumentation are considered blameworthy in Islam.
Correction: This passage shows that argumentation is only blameworthy when done with wrong intentions; it can be commendable when aimed at truth.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what makes argumentation (mira') blameworthy?
A) When it involves difficult questions.
B) When it is done to belittle the opponent and show superiority.
C) When it is done by a child to a parent.
D) When it is done in a loud voice.

Key Takeaway
Argumentation is blameworthy only when the intention is to belittle others and display superiority, as warned by the Prophet.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you argue with someone about religious matters, do you ever catch yourself wanting to 'win' rather than seeking truth? How does this lesson's definition of blameworthy argumentation challenge your behavior? What will you change this week?
?
The hadith warns about making scholars err with difficult questions. Have you ever asked a question to show off your knowledge rather than to learn? Reflect on your intentions and commit to sincerity in seeking knowledge.
?
Are you one of those who delve deeply into trivial matters while neglecting core obligations? How can you balance the pursuit of deep understanding with avoiding nitpicking and fruitless debate?

Commendable Argumentation: A Praiseworthy Act
States the commendable use of argumentation for establishing truth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that argumentation aimed at establishing truth and nullifying falsehood is commendable, even overriding filial obedience.

Core Idea
Argumentation becomes an act of worship when done for the sake of truth.

After examining the blameworthy form, Imam Sanusi now presents the commendable side of argumentation. This passage shows that even a child may correct his parent when truth is at stake, making it a praiseworthy disobedience.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on commendable argumentation
Read the Arabic and translation of the part that begins with 'وَأما إذا كان لإحقاق حق'. Notice the stated purpose.
2
Identify the condition for commendability
What is the intention that makes argumentation praiseworthy? How is it described?
It is to establish truth and nullify falsehood.
3
Reflect on the example of child-parent
The author says it is commendable 'even if from a child to his parent'. Why is this a powerful example?
It shows that truth takes precedence over filial obedience in this context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

His statement: (and like argumentation) is linguistically: extraction; one says 'he argued with so-and-so' when he extracts what he has, and technically: disputing with another regarding what he claims to be correct. And the place of its being blameworthy is when it is to belittle your opponent and show your superiority over him. And it has been reported in the hadith: 'Destroyed are the nitpickers' ... three times; i.e., those who delve deeply into research. And al-Tabarani reported from Thawban as a marfu' hadith: 'There will be in my nation people who will make their scholars err with difficult questions - with damma on 'ayn and fatha on dad, i.e., their difficult ones - those are the worst of my nation.' Commentary
This passage defines mira' (argumentation/disputation) both linguistically and technically, then distinguishes between its blameworthy and commendable forms. Linguistically, it derives from 'extraction'. Technically, it is disputing with someone about what they claim to be correct. The blameworthy form occurs when the intent is to belittle the opponent and demonstrate superiority. The author supports this with hadith warnings against excessive nitpicking and making scholars err with difficult questions. Transition to Tasawwuf and Its Definition
The author concludes the creed section and defines tasawwuf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the transition from creed to tasawwuf in the text and the definition of tasawwuf as purification of the heart.

Core Idea
Tasawwuf is the science of purifying the heart for Allah alone.

This passage marks a shift from discussing matters of belief (aqida) to the inner spiritual work of tasawwuf. The author explains that tasawwuf involves a two-step process: shedding vices and acquiring virtues, and defines it as a science for rectifying the heart. Al-Ghazali's succinct definition clarifies that tasawwuf is about stripping the heart for Allah and recognizing that nothing else truly benefits or harms.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the transition
Notice how the author signals the end of the creed section with 'fa'tamid' and then introduces the theme of character and tasawwuf.
The line 'fa'tamid' signifies reliance on the creed just presented.
2
Distinguish between takhliya and tahliya
The passage describes two stages: divesting from vices (takhliya) and adorning with virtues (tahliya). Identify these in the commentary.
Takhliya uses the letter kha', tahliya uses ha'.
3
Understand al-Ghazali's definition
Read the definition and the clarification about 'belittling what is other than Allah'. Note that it means reliance on Allah alone, not contempt for creation.
The clarification avoids misunderstanding the term 'belittling'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فَاعْتَمِدْ) المقصود منه التكملة، وأشار به المصنف إلى انقضاء فنّ العقائد؛ أي : فاعتمد في العقائد على ما ذكرته ؛ لأنه مذهب أهل السنة والجماعة. التخلق بأخلاق النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وَمَن سار على هَدِيهِ. ١٣٦ - وَكُنْ كَمَا كَانَ خِيارُ الخَلْقِ حَلِيْفَ حِلْمِ تَابِعاً لِلحَقِّ. قوله : (وَكُنْ ... إلخ) هذا من باب التخلص من التخلية - بالخاء المعجمة ـ ؛ أي التخلي من الرذائل التي أشار إليها بقوله : ( واجتنب ... إلخ) إلى التحلية - بالحاء المهملة - ؛ أي: التحلي بالفضائل التي أشار إليها بقوله : (وكن .. إلخ). وقد ذكر المصنف شيئاً من فنّ التصوف ومنه مباحث النميمة وما بعدها من المهلكات فهي تصوف : وعرفوه بأنه : علم بأصول يعرف بها إصلاح القلب وسائر الحواس. وفائدته : إصلاح أحوال الإنسان.. لما فيه من الحث على تصفية الاعتقاد، وكمال الأعمال بالسداد. وقال الغزالي : هو تجريد القلب الله تعالى واحتقار ما سواه أي تخليص القلب الله تعالى واعتقاد أن ما سواه لا ينفع ولا يضرُّ، فلا يعوَّل إلا على الله ؛ والمراد باحتقار ما سواه اعتقاد أنه لا يضرُّ ولا ينفع ؛ وليس المراد به الازدراء والتنقيص.
His statement: 'so rely' — its intent is completion, and the author indicated by it the end of the art of creeds; i.e., rely in creeds on what I have mentioned, for it is the school of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a. Adopting the character of the Prophet, peace be upon him, and those who follow his guidance. 136 — 'And be as were the best of creation, ally of forbearance, follower of the truth.' His statement: 'and be... etc.' — this is from the category of divestment (al-takhliya) — with the letter kha' — i.e., divesting from vices which he indicated in his statement: 'and avoid... etc.' — to adornment (al-tahliya) — with the letter ha' — i.e., adorning with virtues which he indicated in his statement: 'and be... etc.' And the author has mentioned something of the art of tasawwuf, and among it are discussions of gossip and what follows from the destroyers; so it is tasawwuf. And they defined it as: a science by whose principles one knows the rectification of the heart and all the senses. Its benefit: rectification of the states of man, because it contains encouragement to purify belief and perfect deeds with soundness. And al-Ghazali said: It is stripping the heart for Allah, may He be exalted, and belittling what is other than Him — i.e., purifying the heart for Allah and believing that what is other than Him neither benefits nor harms, so one relies only on Allah. And what is meant by belittling what is other than Him is the belief that it neither harms nor benefits; not that it means contempt and disparagement.
Source pages p. 417

Commentary
This passage serves as a transition from the section on creed ('aqa'id) to the section on spiritual purification (tasawwuf). The author explains that the line 'fa'tamid' signals the completion of the creed discussion, urging reliance on the presented doctrines as they represent the school of Ahl al-Sunna. He then introduces the theme of adopting the Prophet's character with a poetic line. The commentary on the poetry explains that this involves two stages: first, self-purification from vices (takhliya), then adornment with virtues (tahliya). The author notes that tasawwuf is the subject of this section, covering topics like gossip and other spiritual destroyers. He provides a formal definition of tasawwuf as a science teaching the rectification of the heart and senses, with the benefit of reforming one's states and encouraging pure belief and good deeds. He then quotes al-Ghazali's definition: 'stripping the heart for Allah and belittling what is other than Him.' He clarifies that 'belittling' here means recognizing that nothing besides Allah truly benefits or harms, not that one should show contempt or disdain for creation. This lesson thus introduces the subject matter and purpose of tasawwuf within the broader work.

Key Terms
التصوف
التخلية
التحلية
تجريد القلب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Tasawwuf's 'belittling what is other than Allah' means showing contempt for people or the world.
Correction: The text clarifies it means believing that nothing other than Allah truly benefits or harms, so one relies solely on Allah. It does not imply contempt.

Checkpoint
According to al-Ghazali's definition cited in the text, what is meant by 'belittling what is other than Allah'?
A) Showing contempt for all creatures
B) Believing that nothing else truly benefits or harms
C) Avoiding all worldly interactions
D) Disparaging non-Muslims

Key Takeaway
Tasawwuf is the spiritual science that purifies the heart for Allah, relying solely on Him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that nothing besides Allah can harm or benefit you, or does your heart still tremble at the opinion of someone powerful? When will you strip that fear from your heart and rely on Him alone?

?
Al-Ghazali said tasawwuf is 'belittling what is other than Allah.' Look at what you spend your thoughts and energy on—how much of it is truly for Allah? Are you willing to let go of even good things if they distract you from Him?

Introduction to Tasawwuf: Purification of the Heart
Concludes beliefs and defines tasawwuf with two definitions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how tasawwuf is defined as a science of heart rectification and its purpose in purifying belief and deeds.

Core Idea
Tasawwuf is the science of purifying the heart for Allah alone.

This lesson marks a transition from the study of beliefs to the inner dimension of Islam: tasawwuf. The commentator explains how the author's previous discussion of vices and virtues naturally leads to the art of spiritual purification. We will read two key definitions that establish tasawwuf as a disciplined science of heart rectification, not mere mysticism.

Guided Path
1
Understand the transition
Notice how the author signals the end of the belief section and introduces tasawwuf as the next subject. The commentator explains that the discussion of backbiting and destructive matters belongs to tasawwuf.
The author uses 'fa'tamid' to conclude and 'wa kun' to begin a new theme.
2
Define tasawwuf as a science
Read the definition: tasawwuf is a knowledge of principles by which the heart and senses are rectified. Its benefit is reforming the human state through purifying belief and perfecting deeds.
This frames tasawwuf as a practical science, not mere theory.
3
Examine al-Ghazali's definition
Al-Ghazali defines tasawwuf as purifying the heart for Allah and despising everything else. The commentary clarifies that 'despising' means recognizing that only Allah benefits or harms, not arrogance toward creation.
This clarifies a common misunderstanding about the term 'despising'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فَاعْتَمِدْ) المقصود منه التكملة، وأشار به المصنف إلى انقضاء فنّ العقائد؛ أي : فاعتمد في العقائد على ما ذكرته؛ لأنه مذهب أهل السنة والجماعة. قوله : (وَكُنْ ... إلخ) إلخ) هذا من باب التخلص من التخلية - بالخاء المعجمة ـ ؛ أي التخلي من الرذائل التي أشار إليها بقوله : ( واجتنب ... إلخ) إلى التحلية - بالحاء المهملة - ؛ أي: التحلي بالفضائل التي أشار إليها بقوله : (وكن .. إلخ). وقد ذكر المصنف شيئاً من فنّ التصوف ومنه مباحث النميمة وما بعدها من المهلكات فهي تصوف : وعرفوه بأنه : علم بأصول يعرف بها إصلاح القلب وسائر الحواس. وفائدته : إصلاح أحوال الإنسان.. لما فيه من الحث على تصفية الاعتقاد، وكمال الأعمال بالسداد. 6 وقال الغزالي : هو تجريد القلب الله تعالى واحتقار ما سواه أي تخليص القلب الله تعالى واعتقاد أن ما سواه لا ينفع ولا يضرُّ، فلا يعوَّل إلا على الله ؛ والمراد باحتقار ما سواه اعتقاد أنه لا يضرُّ ولا ينفع ؛ وليس المراد به الازدراء والتنقيص .
His statement: (فَاعْتَمِدْ): its purpose is completion, and the author indicated by it the conclusion of the art of beliefs; i.e., rely in beliefs on what I have mentioned, for it is the way of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a. His statement: (وَكُنْ ... etc.) this is of the type of detachment from purification—with the dotted kha—i.e., detachment from the vices he indicated by his statement: (واجتنب ... etc.) to adornment—with the undotted ha—i.e., adornment with the virtues he indicated by his statement: (وكن .. etc.). And the author mentioned something of the art of tasawwuf, and among it are the topics of backbiting and what follows from the destructive matters, so they are tasawwuf. And they defined it as: a knowledge of principles by which the rectification of the heart and the rest of the senses is known. Its benefit: rectification of the human state, due to what it contains of urging purification of belief and perfection of deeds with correctness. And al-Ghazali said: It is purifying the heart for Allah Most High and despising what is other than Him, i.e., purifying the heart for Allah Most High and believing that what is other than Him neither benefits nor harms, so one relies only on Allah; and the meaning of despising what is other than Him is believing that it neither harms nor benefits; and the intended meaning is not belittlement and diminishment.

Commentary
This passage serves as a transition from the section on beliefs (al-'aqa'id) to the section on the cultivation of prophetic morals and tasawwuf. The author's statement 'fa'tamid' (so rely) is explained as a completion marker, indicating that the previous material on beliefs is the established doctrine of Ahl al-Sunna. Then the commentator introduces the next line 'wa kun ...' and explains that it is part of the process of tahalli (adornment) after takhliyya (purification). The author then mentions that the previous discussion on backbiting and destructive matters belongs to the art of tasawwuf, and provides a definition: tasawwuf is a science of principles by which the heart and senses are rectified, and its benefit is reforming the human state by purifying belief and perfecting deeds. He then quotes al-Ghazali's definition: it is purifying the heart for Allah and considering everything else insignificant, meaning one believes that only Allah can benefit or harm, so one relies solely on Him. It is clarified that 'despising what is other than Allah' does not mean belittlement, but rather a recognition of their powerlessness.

Who Are the Best of Creation? Interpreting a Poetic Line
Commentator explains the line 'as you were the best of creation' and its applications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the different interpretations of 'best of creation' in this poem and the practical advice on emulating them.

Core Idea
The 'best of creation' includes prophets, scholars, saints—each according to their rank.

This passage from the commentary unpacks a seemingly simple phrase from the poem. The commentator explains the grammar, identifies who is meant, and then draws a powerful practical lesson: we should emulate the best according to our capacity and seek guidance from a righteous shaykh. Let's see how he builds this teaching.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Get a sense of the commentator's style.
Notice the grammatical terms like 'kaf' and 'ba'.
2
Identify the three interpretations of 'best of creation'
The commentator gives three possible referents: specifically the Prophet, all prophets, or everyone with proven goodness. Note which one he prefers.
His preferred view expands the meaning significantly.
3
Understand the distribution of goodness
The passage explains that different people can emulate different aspects of goodness according to their capacity. This makes the teaching applicable to all.
4
Grasp the advice about seeking a shaykh
The commentator adds practical spiritual guidance: emulation under a shaykh is more beneficial. Understand why and how to choose one.
The saying about 'state of one man...' is key.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : كَمَا كَانَ خِيارُ الخَلْقِ أي كن متصفاً بأخلاق مثل الأخلاق التي كان عليها خيار الخلق، فالكاف للتمثيل والتشبيه، ويحتمل أن تكون بمعنى الباء؛ أي: كُنْ متصفاً بالأخلاق التي كان عليها خيار الخلق، والمراد من خيار الخلق نبينا ؛ لأنه ما تفرق في غيره من الخصال الحميدة، فهو الخيار المطلق. ويحتمل أن المراد به الأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام؛ لأنهم خيار الخلق. جمع والأولى أن يُراد به كل من ثبتت له الخيرية، ولو بالنسبة لمن دونه، فيشمله ، ويشمل الأنبياء والعلماء والشهداء والأولياء والزهاد والعباد، ويكون الكلامُ مُوزّعاً باعتبار الأشخاص وأنواع الخير ؛ فمن الناس من له قدرة على صورة مجاهدته ، ومنهم من له قدرة على صورة مجاهدة غيره من الأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام، ومنهم له قدرة على مجاهدة العلماء، وهلم جرا ؛ وإذا كانت المجاهدة على يد شيخ من العارفين كانت أنفع لقولهم : (حال) رجل في ألف رجلٍ أنفعُ من وَغظ ألفِ رجلٍ من في رجل)، فينبغي للشخص أن يلزم شيخاً عارفاً على الكتاب والسنة، بأن يَزنَهُ قبل الأخذ عنه، فإن وجده على الكتاب والسنة لازمه وتأدب معه فعساه يكتسب من حاله ما يكون به صفاء باطنه، والله يتولّى هداه.
His statement: 'as you were the best of creation' — i.e., be adorned with morals like the morals that the best of creation had, so the kaf is for comparison and likeness, and it is possible that it is in the sense of the preposition ba; i.e., 'be adorned with the morals that the best of creation had.' The intended meaning of 'the best of creation' is our Prophet, because good qualities are not scattered in anyone else; he is the absolute best. It is also possible that it means the prophets (peace be upon them) because they are the best of creation. Together, the better view is that it refers to everyone who has proven goodness, even relative to those below him, so it includes him, and includes the prophets, scholars, martyrs, saints, ascetics, and worshippers. The speech is distributed according to persons and types of goodness: some people have ability to emulate his striving, some have ability to emulate the striving of other prophets, some have ability to emulate the striving of scholars, and so forth. And if the striving is under the guidance of a shaykh who is a knower of God, it is more beneficial, because they say: 'The state of one man among a thousand men is more beneficial than the preaching of a thousand men to one man.' So a person should adhere to a shaykh who is a knower of God, upon the Book and Sunnah, by examining him before taking from him. If he finds him upon the Book and Sunnah, he should stick to him and behave with good manners towards him, so that perhaps he may acquire from his state that by which his inner self becomes pure, and God undertakes his guidance.
Source pages p. 418

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the poetic line 'as you were the best of creation'. The commentator begins by parsing the grammar: the kaf is for comparison, meaning 'be adorned with morals like those of the best of creation'. It could also be the ba meaning 'be adorned with the morals that the best of creation had'. He then identifies who 'the best of creation' refers to. The primary meaning is our Prophet Muhammad, because all good qualities are concentrated in him and not scattered in others—he is the absolute best. A secondary interpretation is all the prophets, as they are the best. The commentator then gives the preferred view: it includes everyone who has proven goodness, even relative to those below him, so it includes prophets, scholars, martyrs, saints, ascetics, and worshippers. The line is therefore distributed across persons and types of goodness: each person can emulate according to his capacity—some can emulate the Prophet's striving, others the striving of earlier prophets or of scholars. The commentator then adds an important practical point: striving under a shaykh who is a knower of God is more beneficial, because the spiritual state of one person can affect many. Therefore, one should carefully choose a shaykh who adheres to the Quran and Sunnah, and then adhere to him with proper etiquette, hoping to acquire his spiritual state for inner purification.

Key Terms

الخيرية
مجاهدة
حال
شيخ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many think 'best of creation' refers only to the Prophet Muhammad.
Correction: The commentator's preferred view includes all who have proven goodness, such as prophets, scholars, and saints, each according to their rank.

Checkpoint
According to the commentator's preferred view, who is included in 'the best of creation'?
A) Only the Prophet Muhammad
B) Only the prophets
C) Everyone who has proven goodness, including prophets, scholars, and saints
D) Only the Companions

Key Takeaway
The 'best of creation' is a broad category including prophets, scholars, and saints, and we are encouraged to emulate them according to our ability, especially under a righteous shaykh.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The commentator says the spiritual state (hal) of one righteous person can be more beneficial than the preaching of a thousand. Are you more invested in your own state before God or in telling others what to do? How can you shift your focus to acquiring inner purity this week?
?
You are commanded to seek a shaykh who is upon the Book and Sunnah, and to examine him before taking from him. Have you ever actually scrutinized a teacher's adherence to Quran and Sunnah, or do you follow based on charisma or tradition? Follower of the Truth
Commentator explains 'follower of the truth' with practical conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that being a follower of the truth requires active obedience to God's commands and weighing all actions by the Sharia.

Core Idea
Following the truth means obeying God's commands and avoiding His prohibitions.

The commentator unpacks the phrase 'follower of the truth' from the poem, showing that it is more than a title—it demands concrete action. He clarifies that 'the truth' refers primarily to God Himself, and then to His religion and rulings. The lesson culminates in a practical exhortation to measure every word, deed, and belief against the scale of divine law.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how the commentator moves from linguistic explanation to practical application.
The phrase 'tabi'an lil-haqq' is the third predicate of 'kun' (be).
2
Understand the meaning of 'al-Haqq'
The commentator explains that 'al-Haqq' can mean God or the true religion/rulings. Reflect on why this dual meaning is significant.
God is the ultimate Truth; His commands are true rulings.
3
Identify the condition for following
The passage states you are not a follower of the truth unless you adhere, comply with commands, and avoid prohibitions. Note the Quranic verse quoted.
Verse 59:7 emphasizes taking what the Messenger gives and desisting from what he forbids.
4
Apply the scale of Sharia
The commentator instructs to weigh all words, actions, and beliefs by the Sharia. Consider how this applies to daily life.
Guarding senses and controlling breaths means mindfulness in every moment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (تَابِعاً لِلحَقِّ) أي : وكُنْ تابعاً للحق فهو خبر ثالث لـ (كُنْ) المتقدمة، والمراد بالحق الله تعالى؛ لأن الحق اسمٌ من أسمائه . وفي الكلام حذف مضاف؛ أي: لدين الحق ويحتمل أن المراد به الأحكام الحقة، وحينئذ فلا حاجة لتقدير المضاف . ولا يخفى عليك أيها الموفق ؛ أنك لا تكون تابعاً للحق إلا إذا كنت متمسكاً به، ممتثلاً لأوامره مجتنباً لنواهيه، قال تعالى: ﴿وَمَا انَنكُمُ الرَّسُولُ فَخُذُوهُ وَمَا نَهَنكُمْ عَنْهُ فَانتَهُوا ﴾ [الحشر: ،، فزن جميع أقوالك وأفعالك واعتقاداتك بميزان الشريعة، وعليك بحفظ الحواس وضبط الأنفاس.
His statement: 'follower of the truth' — i.e., 'and be a follower of the truth', so it is a third predicate of the preceding 'be'. And the intended meaning of 'the truth' is God Most High, because 'the Truth' (al-Haqq) is one of His names. In the speech there is an omitted genitive phrase; i.e., 'the religion of truth'. And it is possible that the intended meaning is the true rulings, and then there is no need to assume a genitive phrase. And it is not hidden from you, O the one granted success, that you are not a follower of the truth unless you are adhering to it, complying with its commands, and avoiding its prohibitions. He said, Most High: 'And whatever the Messenger gives you, take it; and whatever he forbids you, desist.' So weigh all your words, actions, and beliefs by the scale of the Sharia, and upon you is to guard your senses and control your breaths.
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This passage explains the phrase 'tabi'an lil-haqq' (follower of the truth). The commentator first notes it is the third predicate of the implied 'be'. He then explains that 'al-Haqq' here primarily means God, as it is one of His names. There is an omitted genitive: it can be read as 'the religion of truth'. Alternatively, it could refer to the true rulings themselves, in which case no addition is needed. The commentator then emphasizes that being a true follower of the truth requires actively adhering to it: complying with God's commands and avoiding His prohibitions. He quotes the Quranic verse (59:7) about taking what the Messenger gives and refraining from what he forbids. He concludes with a practical exhortation: weigh all your words, actions, and beliefs by the scale of the Sharia, and guard your senses and control your breaths (i.e., be mindful and intentional).

Correction: The commentator asserts that you cannot be a follower of the truth unless you actively adhere to it, comply with its commands, and avoid its prohibitions, as evidenced by the Quranic verse.

The Scope of Following the Four Imams
Commentator explains the reason for following predecessors and the scope of obligation to follow the four imams.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scope of the obligation to follow the four mujtahid imams according to Ahl al-Sunnah.

Core Idea
Following the salaf is the source of all good, but the obligation to follow the four imams specifically applies to public rulings, not personal practice.

This passage clarifies a crucial nuance in Sunni methodology: while all good lies in following the predecessors, the consensus that prohibits departing from the four imams is limited to issuing fatwas and judicial rulings. For one's own personal practice, flexibility remains. Let's unpack the commentator's reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Get a feel for the commentator's style.
The Arabic has a typo: 'انْبَاعِ' is likely 'اتِّبَاعِ'.
2
Identify the causal link
Notice how the line 'So every good is in following who preceded' is presented as the reason for the earlier command to be like the best of creation.
The 'fa' here means 'because'.
3
Understand the scope of 'salaf'
The commentator first defines 'who preceded' broadly (prophets, Companions, Followers) but then narrows to the four imams because of the consensus about them.
4
Distinguish public vs. personal practice
The key nuance: the prohibition of departing from the four imams applies only to issuing fatwas and judicial rulings. For one's own worship, imitating other scholars is allowed.
This avoids excessive rigidity.
5
Reflect on the balance
Consider how this teaching balances following the authoritative tradition with practical flexibility for individuals.
This is a hallmark of Sunni methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فَكُلُّ خَيْرٍ فِي انْبَاعِ مَنْ سَلَف هذا عِلَّةٌ للأمر السابق في قوله: (وكن كما كان خيار الخلق ... إلخ)؛ فالمعنى : لأن كلَّ خيرٍ حاصل في اتباع من سلف، فالفاء بمعنى لام التعليل، والمراد بمن سلف من تقدَّم من الأنبياء والصحابة والتابعين وتابعيهم، خصوصاً الأئمة الأربعة المجتهدين الذين انعقد الإجماع على امتناع الخروج عن مذاهبهم في الإفتاء والحكم. وأما عمل الشخص في نفسه فيجوز تقليد غيرهم فيه.
His statement: 'So every good is in following who preceded (man salaf)' — this is a reason for the preceding command in his statement: 'And be as the best of creation were... etc.' So the meaning is: because every good is obtained in following who preceded. So the fa is in the sense of lam al-ta'lil (causal lām). The intended meaning of 'who preceded' are those who came before from among the prophets, Companions, Followers, and those who followed them, especially the four mujtahid imams concerning whom there is consensus on the prohibition of departing from their schools in legal opinions and judgments. As for a person's personal practice, it is permissible to imitate other than them in it.
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This passage explains the concluding line of the poem: 'So every good is in following who preceded, and every evil is in innovating of who came later.' The commentator states that this line is the reason (illa) for the previous commands to be like the best of creation and to be a companion of forbearance and a follower of the truth. The meaning is that all good is obtained by following those who came before. The fa here is the causal fa (like 'because'). 'Who preceded' includes the prophets, the Companions, the Followers, and their followers. The commentator specifically highlights the four mujtahid imams (Abu Hanifa, Malik, al-Shafi'i, Ahmad) because there is consensus that it is impermissible to depart from their schools in matters of issuing fatwas and judicial rulings. However, he adds an important exception: for a person's own personal practice (not issuing fatwas for others), it is permissible to follow other imams (i.e., to do taqlid of someone else outside these four). This clarifies the scope of the obligation to follow the four imams.

Key Terms
اتباع
سلف
إجماع
تقليد
أئمة أربعة
إفتاء
حكم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One must always follow one of the four imams in all actions, including personal worship.
Correction: The prohibition of departing from the four imams applies only to issuing fatwa and judgment; for personal practice, following other scholars is permissible.

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, for what purposes is it prohibited to depart from the four imams?
A) For all personal practices
B) For issuing fatwas and judgments
C) For reciting Quran
D) For spiritual retreats

Key Takeaway
The four imams are authoritative in public rulings, but personal practice allows following other qualified scholars.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you seek religious guidance, do you prioritize the opinion of a scholar who is popularly followed, or do you consider the strength of their evidence? Are you willing to follow a lesser-known scholar if their evidence is stronger? Will you commit to learning the evidence behind the rulings you follow?
?
Think of a personal practice you follow that differs from the four imams. Did you adopt it because it was easier, or because you are convinced it is more correct? Are you ready to change it if you find stronger evidence from the Qur’an and Sunnah?
?
Do you ever judge others for not following the same madhhab as you? How does this lesson’s distinction between public rulings and personal practice challenge your assumptions? Will you strive to respect valid differences among scholars?

Adhering to a Righteous Shaykh
Commentator advises seeking a shaykh upon the Book and Sunnah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the importance of seeking a knowledgeable shaykh who adheres to the Book and Sunnah, and how to benefit from him with good manners.

Core Idea
The true shaykh is a guide on the path of Allah, not a blind leader.

In this passage, the commentator gives practical advice for every seeker of truth: we must carefully choose a shaykh who himself follows the Quran and Sunnah, then learn from his example with good manners. This is the first step toward inner purification.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation to grasp the commentator's advice.
Notice the sequence: evaluate, adhere, show good manners.
2
Identify the criteria for choosing a shaykh
The passage requires that the shaykh be 'aarif (knowledgeable) and upon the Book and Sunnah. The seeker must weigh him before taking from him.
This prevents blind following.
3
Reflect on the purpose of adherence
The goal is to acquire the shaykh's state for inner clarity (safaa' batini). This shows the spiritual dimension of learning.
Allah ultimately guides.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في رجل)، فينبغي للشخص أن يلزم شيخاً عارفاً على الكتاب والسنة، بأن يَزنَهُ قبل الأخذ عنه، فإن وجده على الكتاب والسنة لازمه وتأدب معه فعساه يكتسب من حاله ما يكون به صفاء باطنه، والله يتولّى هداه.
قوله : (حَلِيْفَ حِلْمٍ) أي : وكن حليف حِلْمٍ، فهو خبر ثان، لكن في قوله: (وكن كما كان خيار الخلق)، والحليف بمعنى المحالف والملازم، فهو فعيل بمعنى مفاعل، والحلم بمعنى تحمل مشاق عباد الله بحيث لا يستفزك الشيطان، ولا الهوى ولا يحرِّكُكَ الغضب؛ فالشجاع ليس بالصُّرَعَة، إنما الشجاع من يملك نفسه عند الغضب، وإنما خَصَّ الناظم الحلم بالذكر مع دخوله في عموم ما كان عليه خيار الخلق اهتماماً به ولأنه وصف جامع لأوصاف الخير، لكن الحلم فيما يُغضب الله مذموم.
قوله : (تَابِعاً لِلحَقِّ) أي : وكُنْ تابعاً للحق فهو خبر ثالث لـ (كُنْ) المتقدمة، والمراد بالحق الله تعالى؛ لأن الحق اسمٌ من أسمائه .
وفي الكلام حذف مضاف؛ أي: لدين الحق ويحتمل أن المراد به الأحكام الحقة، وحينئذ فلا حاجة لتقدير المضاف .
ولا يخفى عليك أيها الموفق ؛ أنك لا تكون تابعاً للحق إلا إذا كنت متمسكاً به، ممتثلاً لأوامره مجتنباً لنواهيه، قال تعالى: ﴿وَمَا آتَاكُمُ الرَّسُولُ فَخُذُوهُ وَمَا نَهَاكُمْ عَنْهُ فَانتَهُوا ﴾ [الحشر: 7]، فزن جميع أقوالك وأفعالك واعتقاداتك بميزان الشريعة، وعليك بحفظ الحواس وضبط الأنفاس.
(Concerning a man?) So it is incumbent upon a person to adhere to a knowledgeable shaykh upon the Book and the Sunna, that he weigh him before taking from him. If he finds him upon the Book and the Sunna, he should adhere to him and show good manners with him, so that perhaps he may acquire from his state that by which his inner self becomes clear. And God undertakes his guidance.
His saying: (حَلِيْفَ حِلْمٍ) i.e. And be a close friend of forbearance, so it is a second predicate, but in his saying: (And be as the best of creation were), and al-ḥalīf (close friend) means the confederate and the constant companion, so it is faʿīl in the sense of mufāʿal, and al-ḥilm (forbearance) means bearing the hardships of God's servants such that Satan does not provoke you, nor desire, nor anger stir you. For the brave is not the wrestler; rather the brave is the one who controls himself at the time of anger. And the poet specifically mentioned forbearance even though it is included in the generality of what the best of creation were upon, due to attention to it and because it is a comprehensive attribute of the attributes of goodness. But forbearance in what angers God is blameworthy.
His saying: (تَابِعاً لِلحَقِّ) i.e. And be a follower of the Truth, so it is a third predicate for the implicit 'be', and by al-ḥaqq (the Truth) is meant God Most High, because 'the Truth' is one of His names. And in the speech there is an omitted genitive; i.e. (the religion) of truth. And it is possible that by it is meant the true rulings, and then there is no need to estimate the genitive.
And it is not hidden from you, O the one granted success, that you will not be a follower of the Truth unless you are holding fast to it, complying with its commands, avoiding its prohibitions. He said, Most High: {And whatever the Messenger gives you, take it, and whatever he forbids you from, desist} (al-Hashr 7). So measure all your words, deeds, and beliefs by the scale of the Sharia. And upon you is to guard the senses and control the breaths.
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This passage is a teacherly admonition and commentary on the line 'And be as the best of creation were'. It begins with practical advice: a person should seek a knowledgeable shaykh who adheres to the Book and Sunna, evaluate him before following him, and if found sound, adhere to him and learn from his state for inner purification. The author then explains the phrase 'حليف حلم' (companion of forbearance). He notes that 'حليف' denotes a confederate or constant companion, and 'حلم' means bearing hardships patiently, resisting Satan, desire, and anger. He highlights that true courage is not physical strength but self-control during anger, citing a hadith. The poet specifically singled out forbearance because it is a comprehensive virtue, but warns that forbearance is blameworthy when it involves tolerating what angers God. Next, he explains 'تابعا للحق' (follower of the Truth). 'الحق' is a name of God, and it may also refer to the true religion or rulings. He emphasises that being a true follower requires adhering to God's commands and prohibitions, quoting the Quranic verse to accept what the Messenger gives and abstain from what he forbids. Finally, he exhorts the reader to weigh all words, deeds, and beliefs by the scale of Sharia, and to guard the senses and control one's breaths—meaning mindfulness in all actions.

Key Terms
شيخ
عارف
الكتاب
السنة
تأدب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think following a shaykh means blind imitation without evaluation.
Correction: The passage instructs to weigh the shaykh first against the Book and Sunnah before adherence.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what must a person do before taking from a shaykh?
A) Adhere to him immediately
B) Weigh him against the Book and Sunnah
C) Ask for miracles
D) Follow him unconditionally

Key Takeaway
A seeker of truth must evaluate a shaykh by the Quran and Sunnah, then adhere with good manners for inner purification.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever evaluated a shaykh or teacher by the Quran and Sunnah before committing to follow them? What would you do if you realized a respected teacher contradicts the Quran?
?
Do you show good manners (adab) to your shaykh as an act of worship, or do you take him for granted? How might neglecting adab affect your inner clarity?
?
Is your heart clear (safa batini) because of your relationship with a righteous guide, or have you been content with a surface-level connection? What step will you take today to acquire from your shaykh's state?

The Virtue of Forbearance and True Courage
Commentary on the meaning of forbearance and true courage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of 'companion of forbearance', the true definition of courage, and the boundary of praiseworthy forbearance.

Core Idea
True courage is self-control at anger, not physical strength.

The commentator now unpacks the phrase 'حليف حلم' (companion of forbearance). He explains that forbearance is a comprehensive virtue, but warns that it must not be applied in matters that anger Allah. This lesson distinguishes between praiseworthy and blameworthy forbearance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and translation to understand the definition of forbearance and the hadith on courage.
Pay attention to the linguistic note on 'حليف'.
2
Examine the definition of forbearance
Forbearance is described as bearing hardships without being provoked by Satan, desire, or anger.
It involves controlling emotions.
3
Note the correction about true courage
The passage cites the hadith that the brave is not the wrestler but the one who controls himself at anger.
This refutes a common misconception.
4
Understand the exception
Forbearance is blameworthy when it involves tolerating what angers Allah. This sets a limit.
Not all forbearance is good.

Following the Truth in All Matters
Explanation of following the Truth and practical submission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand what it means to be a follower of the Truth and how to apply the Sharia to all aspects of life.

Core Idea
Being a follower of Allah's truth means measuring every action by the scale of the Sharia.

The commentator now explains the phrase 'تابعا للحق' (follower of the Truth). He identifies 'al-Haqq' as a name of Allah and emphasizes that true following requires holding fast to His commands and prohibitions. The lesson concludes with a powerful exhortation to weigh all words, deeds, and beliefs by the Sharia and to guard one's senses and breaths.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the grammatical explanation of 'تابعا للحق' and the omitted genitive.
The commentator offers two interpretations.
2
Understand the condition for being a follower
The passage states that one cannot be a follower of Truth without holding fast to it and obeying its commands and prohibitions.
Quoting Quran 59:7.
3
Apply the scale of Sharia
The commentator commands to weigh all words, deeds, and beliefs by the Sharia, and to guard the senses and control breaths.
This is a comprehensive directive.

beginner

Following the Salaf: The Source of All Good
Commentator explains the causative link in the couplet on Salaf and later generations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of the couplet 'All good is in following the Salaf, and all evil in the innovation of later generations' and its significance in Islamic methodology.

Core Idea
All good follows the Salaf; all evil follows innovation.

The commentator explains a famous couplet that encapsulates the Sunni approach to guidance. This lesson unpacks the meaning of the couplet, identifying who the Salaf are and why following them is tied to good, while innovation leads to evil.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to understand the couplet and the commentator's explanation.
Pay attention to the causal language used by the commentator.
2
Identify the causal reasoning
Notice that each hemistich is a cause ('illa) for a command or prohibition in the preceding verse.
The fā' in 'fakullu khayrin' functions as the lām of causation.
3
Understand who the Salaf are
The commentator lists the groups included in 'man salaf' from prophets to the four imams. Reflect on the special status of the four imams.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فَكُلُّ خَيْرٍ فِي اتْبَاعِ مَنْ سَلَف) هذا عِلَّةٌ للأمر السابق في قوله: (وكن كما كان خيار الخلق ... إلخ)؛ فالمعنى : لأن كلَّ خيرٍ حاصل في اتباع من سلف، فالفاء بمعنى لام التعليل، والمراد بمن سلف من تقدَّم من الأنبياء والصحابة والتابعين وتابعيهم، خصوصاً الأئمة الأربعة المجتهدين الذين انعقد الإجماع على امتناع الخروج عن مذاهبهم في الإفتاء والحكم. وأما عمل الشخص في نفسه فيجوز تقليد غيرهم فيه.
قوله : (وَكُلُّ شَرٍّ فِي ابْتِدَاعِ مَنْ خَلَف) هذا عِلَّةٌ لما تضمنه الأمر السابق من النهي، والتقدير : ولا تكن كما كان عليه شرار الخلق؛ لأنَّ كلَّ شَرِّ حاصل في ابتداع من خلف ؛ أي: مَنْ تأخَّر من الخلف السيئ الذين أضاعوا الصلوات، واتبعوا الشهوات. واعلم أن البدعة تعتريها الأحكام الخمسة :
فتارة تكون واجبةً ؛ كضبط المصاحف والشرائع إذا خيف عليها الضياع. وتارة تكون محرمةٌ ؛ كالمكس وسائر المحدثات المنافية للقواعد الشرعية.
وتارة تكون مندوبةٌ ؛ كصلاة التراويح جماعة، ولذلك قال سيدنا عمر رضي الله عنه في التراويح (نعمت البدعة هي).
وتارة تكون مكروهةً ؛ كزخرفة المساجد وتزويق المصاحف.
وتارة تكون مباحةً؛ كاتخاذ المناخل للدقيق؛ ففي الآثار: «إن أول شيء أحدثه الناس بعد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اتخاذ المناخل، وإنما كانت مباحةٌ ؛ لأن لين العيش وإصلاحه من المباحات، فوسائله مباحة.
His saying: (فَكُلُّ خَيْرٍ فِي اتْبَاعِ مَنْ سَلَف) i.e. For every good is in following those who preceded (the salaf). This is a cause for the previous command in his saying: (And be as the best of creation were ... etc.); so the meaning is: because every good occurs in following those who preceded. So the fā' is in the sense of the lām of causation. And by 'those who preceded' is meant those who came before among the prophets, Companions, Followers, and their followers, especially the four mujtahid imams concerning whom there is consensus on the prohibition of departing from their schools in issuing fatwas and judgment. As for a person's own individual practice, it is permissible to imitate other than them in it.
His saying: (وَكُلُّ شَرٍّ فِي ابْتِدَاعِ مَنْ خَلَف) i.e. And every evil is in the innovation of those who came later. This is a cause for what the previous command contains of prohibition. The estimate: and do not be as the evil of creation were, because every evil occurs in the innovation of those who came later; i.e. those who came later from the evil successors who neglected the prayers and followed desires. And know that innovation (bid'a) is subject to the five rulings:
Sometimes it is obligatory, like compiling the copies of the Qur'an (maṣāḥif) and the laws if it is feared that they may be lost.
Sometimes it is forbidden, like the unjust tax (maks) and all newly introduced matters that contradict the legal principles.
Sometimes it is recommended, like performing Tarawih prayer in congregation, and therefore our master Umar (may God be pleased with him) said concerning Tarawih: "Excellent bid'a this is."
Sometimes it is disliked, like decorating mosques and embellishing copies of the Qur'an.
Sometimes it is permissible, like adopting sieves for flour. For in the traditions: "The first thing the people introduced after the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) was the adoption of sieves." And it was only permissible because ease of living and its improvement are from permissible matters, so its means are permissible.
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the couplet: 'فكل خير في اتباع من سلف وكل شر في ابتداع من خلف' (All good is in following the predecessors and all evil in innovation of later generations). The commentator explains that the first hemistich is a cause for the earlier command to be like the best of creation; the fā' (fa) is causal. 'من سلف' (those who preceded) includes prophets, Companions, Followers, and their followers, specifically the four mujtahid imams (Abu Hanifa, Malik, Shafi'i, Ahmad) — there is consensus that it is impermissible to depart from their schools in fatwa and judgment. However, for one's personal practice, it is permissible to imitate other scholars. The second hemistich is a cause for the implied prohibition in the earlier command; the estimate is 'do not be like the evil of creation'. 'من خلف' (later ones) refers to the evil successors who neglected prayers and followed desires. Then the commentator states a key principle: innovation (bid'a) can be subject to the five legal rulings. He gives examples: wajib: compiling the Qur'an and laws; haram: unjust tax (maks) and any innovations contradicting Sharia; mandub: Tarawih in congregation (citing Umar's approval); makruh: decorating mosques and embellishing Qur'ans; mubah: using sieves for flour (citing a tradition that this was the first innovation after the Prophet, but it is permissible because it facilitates permissible ease). This shows that bid'a is not always sinful; it is judged by its conformity to Sharia objectives.

Key Terms
سلف
خلف
أئمة أربعة
اتباع
ابتداع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Following the Salaf is just a matter of historical preference.
Correction: The passage shows it is a causative link: all good lies in it, and it is obligatory to follow the four imams in fatwa by consensus.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on departing from the schools of the four imams in issuing fatwas?
A) Permissible
B) Prohibited by consensus
C) Recommended
D) Disliked

Key Takeaway
All good is in following the Salaf, and all evil in innovation—this is the core of Sunni methodology.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The lesson teaches that all good is in following the Salaf and all evil in innovation. Ask yourself: is there any practice in my daily worship that I follow without evidence from the Salaf? Will I muster the courage to investigate and abandon it today?
?
The Salaf are described as those who were obedient and devoted, while the evil later generations neglected prayers and followed desires. Where in my life have I been neglecting an obligatory act of worship or chasing a desire contrary to the Salaf's path? What is one concrete step I will take this week to realign myself?
?
If I truly believe that every good is in the way of the Salaf, what teaching of theirs have I been ignoring or avoiding? How will I change my schedule or priorities to implement that specific teaching starting now?

The Five Rulings on Religious Innovation (Bid'ah)
Commentator lists the five rulings that can apply to bid'ah with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that bid'ah (innovation in religion) is not always sinful, but can carry any of the five legal rulings depending on its nature and purpose.

Core Idea
Bid'ah can be obligatory, forbidden, recommended, disliked, or permissible.

Many Muslims assume that any innovation in religion is automatically sinful. This lesson, based on the commentator's classification, shows that bid'ah is subject to the five juridical categories, with clear examples from Islamic practice.

Guided Path
1
Read the classification
Read the Arabic passage listing the five rulings. Note the examples for each category.
2
Examine each example
For each of the five rulings, understand why the example fits that category based on its benefit or harm.
Compiling Quran is obligatory to preserve religion; unjust taxes are forbidden.
3
Understand the principle
Realize that bid'ah is judged by its means and ends. Permissible worldly innovations are fine; religious innovations must align with Sharia.
Umar's endorsement of Tarawih shows that beneficial innovations can be commendable.

The Five Rulings of Bid'ah (Innovation)
Commentator enumerates the five legal rulings that can apply to bid'ah with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that bid'ah (innovation) can fall under any of the five legal rulings depending on its nature, and that not all innovation is blameworthy.

Core Idea
Innovation in religion can be obligatory, forbidden, recommended, disliked, or permissible.

Many people assume that every innovation in religion is automatically forbidden. However, scholars of Islamic law recognise that bid'ah is not a single monolith; it is subject to the same five rulings as any other action. This passage from the commentary on the Jawharat al-Tawhid clarifies this nuance by enumerating each ruling with concrete examples.

Guided Path
1
Context: Evil in innovation of successors
Read the opening lines where the commentator explains that the preceding command warns against being like the evil successors who introduced harmful innovations.
This sets the stage that not all innovation is blameworthy—only that which leads to evil.
2
Identify the five rulings
Locate each of the five rulings: obligatory, forbidden, recommended, disliked, and permissible. Note the example given for each.
The commentator provides a specific historical or practical example for each category.
3
Reflect on the implications
Consider why the permissibility of some innovations (like sieves) might seem surprising. The commentator explains that means to a permissible end are also permissible.
This shows that bid'ah is judged by its compatibility with the law, not by mere novelty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وَكُلُّ شَرٌّ فِي ابْتِدَاعِ مَنْ خَلَفْ هذا عِلَّةٌ لما تضمنه الأمر السابق من النهي، والتقدير : ولا تكن كما كان عليه شرار الخلق؛ لأنَّ كلَّ شَرِّ حاصل في ابتداع من خلف ؛ أي: مَنْ تأخَّر من الخلف السيئ الذين أضاعوا الصلوات، واتبعوا الشهوات. واعلم أن البدعة تعتريها الأحكام الخمسة : فَتَارَةً تَكُونُ وَاجِبَةً؛ كضبط المصاحف والشرائع إذا خيف عليها الضياع. وَتَارَةً تَكُونُ مُحَرَّمَةً؛ كالمكس وسائر المحدثات المنافية للقواعد الشرعية. وَتَارَةً تَكُونُ مَنْدُوبَةً؛ كصلاة التراويح جماعة، ولذلك قال سيدنا عمر رضي عنه في التراويح (نعمت البدعة هي). وَتَارَةً تَكُونُ مَكْرُوهَةً؛ كزخرفة المساجد وتزويق المصاحف. وَتَارَةً تَكُونُ مُبَاحَةً؛ كاتخاذ المناخل للدقيق؛ ففي الآثار: «إن أول شيء أحدثه الناس بعد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اتخاذ المناخل، وإنما كانت مباحةٌ؛ لأن لين العيش وإصلاحه من المباحات، فوسائله مباحة.
His saying: (And every evil is in the innovation of those who came after) This is a reason for what the preceding command contained of prohibition, and the estimation is: Do not be like the evil of creation were; because every evil that occurs is in the innovation of those who came later, meaning: those who came after from the evil successors who neglected the prayers and followed desires. And know that bid'ah (innovation) is subject to the five rulings: sometimes it is obligatory, like compiling the mushafs (Qur'anic manuscripts) and the laws when there is fear of their loss. And sometimes it is forbidden, like the miks (unlawful tax) and all other innovations contrary to the legal principles. And sometimes it is recommended, like the tarawih prayer in congregation; and for that our master Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, said concerning tarawih: 'What an excellent innovation this is.' And sometimes it is disliked, like ornamenting mosques and embellishing mushafs. And sometimes it is permissible, like taking sieves for flour; for in the traditions: 'The first thing that people innovated after the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, was the taking of sieves.' And it was only permissible because the softening of life and its improvement is from the permissible things, so its means are permissible.
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This passage is a classification of bid'ah into five legal rulings. The commentator first explains the preceding verse: 'Every evil is in the innovation of those who came after.' He clarifies that this refers to the evil successors who neglected prayers and pursued desires. Then he introduces the key point: bid'ah is subject to the five rulings of Islamic law. These are: (1) Obligatory, exemplified by compiling the Qur'an and legal rulings when loss is feared. (2) Forbidden, like the miks (unlawful tax) and any innovation contradicting the sharia. (3) Recommended, like the tarawih prayer in congregation, as Umar's statement 'What an excellent innovation this is' indicates. (4) Disliked, like ornate mosques and embellished Qur'ans. (5) Permissible, like using sieves for flour, which was the first innovation after the Prophet, and it is permitted because its end (better living) is permissible. The commentator thus shows that not every innovation is blameworthy; the ruling depends on the innovation's compatibility with the law.

Key Terms
بدعة
أحكام خمسة
واجبة
محرمة
مندوبة
مكروهة
مباحة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All innovation in religion is unlawful and blameworthy.
Correction: The passage shows that bid'ah is subject to five legal rulings: obligatory, forbidden, recommended, disliked, and permissible. Some innovations are necessary or commendable, like compiling the Qur'an and tarawih prayer.

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what determines whether an innovation is blameworthy or not?
A) Its time of occurrence
B) Its ruling under the five legal categories
C) Whether it was done by the Salaf
D) The intention of the innovator

Key Takeaway
Bid'ah is not uniformly blameworthy; its ruling depends on its conformity with the five legal categories.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
What 'nice' religious practice have you been hesitant to adopt because you thought it might be bid'ah? In light of this passage, how will you evaluate it using the five categories?
?
Umar called Tarawih an 'excellent innovation.' Is there any practice in your community that you have dismissed as bid'ah without considering whether it might be recommended or even obligatory? What step will you take to re-evaluate it?
?
The passage shows that some innovations are necessary to protect the deen. What aspect of your faith or practice is at risk today due to negligence, and what practical innovation (in the sense of a new method) could you adopt to safeguard it?

The Prophet's Guidance and Its Exceptions
Commentator explains the general rule and three exceptions to the Prophet's guidance being preponderant.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the general principle that the Prophet's guidance is preferred and the three exceptions where it is not a binding precedent.

Core Idea
Not every action of the Prophet is a binding sunna; some are abrogated, permissive, or exclusive.

The commentator expands on the line from the poem, explaining that while the Prophet's guidance in sayings, actions, and beliefs is generally superior to others, there are important exceptions. This passage clarifies which of his actions are not meant as general precedents, helping us avoid misunderstanding the scope of his sunna.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic source and its English translation to get the overall sense of the commentary.
2
Identify the general rule
The commentator states that every guidance of the Prophet is preponderant. Understand this as the default ruling.
3
Find the three exceptions
Look for the words 'بخلاف ما نسخ', 'وما قصد به مجرد بيان الجواز', and 'وما كان مختصا' – these introduce the three exceptions.
The exceptions are: abrogated acts, acts indicating mere permissibility, and acts unique to him.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why distinguishing these exceptions matters for correctly following the Prophet's sunna.
Not all actions are meant to be emulated; some were temporary or specific.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وَكُلُّ هَدْيِ لِلنَّبِيِّ قَدْ رَجَحْ) أي : وكلُّ هَدْي منسوب للنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قد رَجَعَ على ما لم ينسب له من الأقوال والأفعال والاعتقادات، فأفضل الأحوال أحواله التي لم تُنسخ ، وليس المقصود بها مجرد بيان الجواز، ولا مما قام الدليل علی اختصاصه به ، بخلاف ما نُسخ كقيام الليل كله، وما قصد به مجرد بیان الجواز كوضوئه مرَّةٌ مرَّةٌ، وما كان مُختَصّاً به عليه الصلاة والسلام؛ كتزوجه أكثر من أربع.
His saying: (And every guidance of the Prophet has been preponderant) means: Every guidance attributed to the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, has excelled over what is not attributed to him of sayings, actions, and beliefs. So the most excellent states are his states that were not abrogated. And the intent with them is not merely to indicate permissibility, nor is it from what evidence has established as being specific to him. Contrary to what was abrogated, such as standing for prayer all night; and what was intended merely to indicate permissibility, such as his wudu once each; and what was specific to him, upon him be peace and blessings, such as his marriage to more than four.
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the line: 'And every guidance of the Prophet has been preponderant.' The commentator clarifies that 'guide' means anything attributable to the Prophet—sayings, actions, or beliefs—and it is superior to anything not attributable to him. However, he specifies that the best of the Prophet's states are those that were not abrogated. Furthermore, some of his actions were not meant as binding precedents: some only indicated permissibility (like doing wudu once each), and some were specific to him (like marrying more than four wives). Thus, the general rule is that the Prophet's guidance is preferred, but not every action is a mandatory or recommended precedent.

Key Terms

بيان الجواز
اختصاص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Every action of the Prophet is a binding sunna.
Correction: The passage clarifies that some actions were abrogated, some merely indicated permissibility, and some were specific to him, thus not all actions are binding precedents.

Checkpoint
What does the commentator exclude from the general principle that the Prophet's guidance is preponderant?
A) All actions of the Prophet
B) Actions that were abrogated, merely indicated permissibility, or were specific to him
C) Only abrogated actions
D) Actions of the Companions

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's guidance is generally preferred, but three categories—abrogated, permissive, and exclusive actions—are not binding precedents.
